The transient is discarded on a `timeStore` **frame-INT** change ONLY (the Blender depsgraph re-eval model, D-149-2) ‚Äî selection/undo/Auto-Key-toggle do NOT clear it. It is persisted only on an explicit key (the NPanel diamond per-param, K/I whole-transform), via the EXISTING insert paths (`keyParamFromTransient` ‚Üí `dispatchFirstKeyComposite`/`mutator.timeline.keyframe`), then the slot is cleared.

**Why it matters:** the transient is "a one-frame un-persisted keyframe". Three traps without this invariant pinned: (1) treating it as a DAG mutation (an Op or `setParam`) re-introduces the H36 double-write on an animated source ‚Äî it must be V1-EXEMPT, held by construction (the OFF branch `return true` already skips the caller's raw write). (2) overlaying it on render but not read (or vice-versa, or with different precedence/sample-time) is the [[H40]] render‚âÝread drift ‚Äî solved by the ONE shared `overlayTransients`. (3) mutating the `edits` Map in place instead of producing a NEW Map breaks the subscribed selectors (the render dirty-check + the orange indicator never fire ‚Äî the [[B12]] snapshot-not-subscribed class). The clear-trigger MUST compare the derived frame INT, not seconds, or a sub-frame jitter wipes the in-progress edit (the W9/[[V20]] frame-INT discipline). The orange field color (`text-warn`, TOP of the diamond precedence) is the MANDATORY non-silent indicator that REPLACES the removed Auto-Key-OFF reject alert (FLAG-A): without it a held edit would vanish on scrub silently ‚Äî the exact #68/#77 "snaps right back" class the alert existed to kill.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#149, 2026-06-04). `src/app/stores/transientEditStore.ts` (multi-slot Map, new-Map-every-write, module-init frame-INT subscription ‚Üí `clearAll`, clearAll/clear no-op when empty so playback churn stays zero); `src/app/overlayTransients.ts` (the one primitive, reuses the exported `writeAt` from `src/nodes/AnimationLayer.ts`); `src/app/animate/autoKeyCommit.ts` (`routeAnimatedGrab` OFF branch ‚Üí `transientEditStore.set`; `keyParamFromTransient` the shared commit fork); `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` (`AnimationLayerR` overlay + transients in the dirty-check tuple, H40 form 2); `src/app/resolveEvaluatedTransform.ts` (C1 overlay) + `src/app/resolveEvaluatedParam.ts` (C2, channel `.sample()` not re-interp); `src/app/NPanel.tsx` (orange + diamond commit); `src/app/KeyboardShortcuts.tsx` (K/I whole-transform).

**Enforcement:** `transientEditStore.test.ts` (multi-slot, frame-INT clear, sub-frame no-clear, subscribe-fires/new-ref); `overlayTransients.test.ts` (transform + nested overlay, identity-on-no-match, base untouched); `routeAnimatedGrab.transient.test.ts` (held + ZERO ops + no alert); `resolveEvaluatedParam.test.ts` (channel `.sample()` + transient override + grep gate banning interp math). **Observed live** (Lokayata, [[H40]] boundary-pair, PAUSED): `tests/e2e/p149-transient-boundary-pair.spec.ts` (C3 rendered position == resolver == transient `[9,0,0]`; C4 rendered material == resolver, channel `#808080==#808080` AND transient `#ff0000==#ff0000`), `p149-clear-on-scrub.spec.ts` (edit‚Üíscrub‚Üícurve `x=3`, transient gone; sub-frame survives), `p149-commit.spec.ts` (diamond + K key the typed transient, source byte-unchanged H36, persists across scrub), `p149-four-color.spec.ts` (gray/green/yellow/orange + multi-slot + commit/scrub clears); perf-fox `commits=0` over 4s playback (the subscribed selector is paused-only safe, [[H48]]). Cross-ref [[V1]] (the EXEMPTION ‚Äî same shelf as timeStore/autoKeyStore), [[V20]] (AnimationLayerR stays the sole TRS writer; overlay applied INSIDE it), [[V29]] (the resolver stays the one read producer; transient is a new BAND not a new resolver), [[H40]] (render==read, the one-band-two-callers enforcement), [[H36]] (non-Op non-setParam ‚Üí zero double-write), [[B12]] (new-Map subscribed selector), dharana [[B1.1]]/[[B14]]. REF: issue #149; the bundled Blender manual `animation/introduction.rst:43-56`, `keyframes/editing.rst:36-39`, `bpy.types.Depsgraph.rst:10-13` (the two-layer base/evaluated contract); `~/.anvideck/projects/basher/ref/GROUND_TRUTH_BLENDER_KEYING.md`; `.planning/phases/149-transient-edit-keyframing/{CONTEXT,RESEARCH,PLAN}.md`.

## V32 ‚Äî The material model is a renderer-agnostic IR; the renderer is a compile target

**Statement:** Basher OWNS its material representation as a serializable, renderer-agnostic IR (OpenPBR-named, lobe-grouped). A renderer (THREE `MeshPhysicalMaterial` on WebGL now; a TSL `NodeMaterial` on WebGPU in v0.7) is reached ONLY through a single pure adapter (`openpbrToThree` ‚Äî the one mapping site, [[V29]] N√óM-drift guard). Wherever a material is persisted, edited, undone, or diffed, it is the IR ‚Äî NEVER a THREE material object and NEVER TSL. The IR stays COMPLETE (all OpenPBR lobes stored, off at weight 0); the WebGL compiler emits only the representable subset and tags the rest `unsupported-in-webgl`.

**Scope:** every material datum ‚Äî the widened `InlineMaterialSpec`, `MaterialValue`/`BakedMaterialSpec` (bridged, NOT renamed), `EvaluatedMesh.material`, the v0.7 material graph. **Breaks when:** someone tries to make TSL or a THREE material the source of truth ‚Äî source-verified IMPOSSIBLE (`Fn()` is a JS closure with no serialize; `Node.serialize()` has no type-registry to rebuild from cold JSON; the official three.js "TSL editor" is a text editor, not a graph persister). Type: STRUCTURAL.

**Why it matters:** the load-bearing invariant behind the whole v0.6‚Üív0.7 material arc (THESIS ¬ß747 "Basher owns the material-graph IR; TSL/WGSL is a compile target"). Three traps it pins: (1) adopting WebGPU/TSL "to get OpenPBR" is a category error ‚Äî `MeshPhysicalNodeMaterial` has the SAME lobes as the WebGL material, three.js ships no OpenPBR closure, so renderer choice is orthogonal to material fidelity (real OpenPBR SSS etc. needs hand-authored TSL regardless of renderer). (2) Persisting a THREE/TSL object as the document ‚Äî un-round-trippable; undo/determinism break. (3) Inlining the IR‚ÜíTHREE mapping in N renderers ‚Äî [[V29]] drift; the adapter must be the ONE site (BakedMeshR's MeshPhysicalMaterial build is the reference to mirror, not copy). MaterialX is the INTERCHANGE boundary (`.mtlx` I/O, v0.7), never the live editing IR (verbose, surface-biased; three.js's loader covers only `standard_surface`).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED for PRIMITIVES (v0.6 #2, issue #178, 2026-06-07 ‚Äî W0-W5 on branch `feat/v06.2-material-editing`): the IR is `InlineMaterialSpec` (widened, `src/nodes/types.ts`); the ONE adapter is `openpbrToThree` (`src/app/material/openpbrToThree.ts`, grep-gated); the one leaf renderer is `usePrimitiveMaterial` (`SceneFromDAG.tsx`); migration v2‚Üív3 + the V10/H14 three-layer guard live in `src/nodes/materialSchema.ts`; texture maps round-trip through OPFS (`attachMapFromFile`). per-submesh glTF (W6) SHIPPED (per-`(child,slotIndex)` override). v0.7 still adds the TSL backend + React-Flow editor "build-B". **v0.6 #3 EXTENSION (issue #181, 2026-06-07):** the IR gained `uvTransform {tiling,offset,rotation}` ‚Äî still IR-owned, still compiled through the ONE `openpbrToThree` adapter (now emits `uvTransform`), applied in `usePrimitiveMaterial` to the cloned map textures. v3‚Üív4 node migration at IDENTITY (V10/H14 span unchanged). Confirms the invariant scales: a new material datum is added to the IR + the one adapter, never to a renderer object. Cross-refs [[V29]] (one EvaluatedMesh face / one read producer), [[V9]] (materials are data not code), [[V10]]/[[H14]] (the widen is a migration ‚Üí IDENTITY-default guard at every consumer; the paramPath rename's full span = [[H74]]), [[V20]]/[[H36]] (one material writer), [[H76]] (clone shared textures before the per-material uvTransform), [[V33]] (UV display sibling), dharana [[B19]], DCC-reference ¬ß11a. REF: memory `project_material_architecture.md` + `session_2026-06-07_v062-w0-w5-shipped.md`; `.planning/phases/v06.2-material-texture-editing/{CONTEXT,RESEARCH,PLAN}.md` + `.planning/phases/v06.3-uv-texture-placement/{CONTEXT,PLAN}.md`; commits `6b43dda`/`6551617`/`ff5776e`/`4d91274`/`674d3d0`/`877185a`/`02d1668`; THESIS ¬ß58/¬ß59/¬ß741/¬ß747.

## V33 ‚Äî A mesh's UV layout is a READ-ONLY display projection, extracted by ONE pure function, populated eagerly only for SYNC-available geometry

**Statement:** the UV layout shown in the UVEditor is a READ-ONLY projection of a mesh's `BufferGeometry.uv` attribute (THESIS ¬ß58 item 3 ‚Äî "view + transform, not surgery"; per-vertex/seam/unwrap stays in Blender via the glTF round-trip). It is built by ONE pure function `extractUVIslands(geometry)` (`src/app/uvIslands.ts`) ‚Äî islands = topological connected components (faces sharing vertex indices), a DISPLAY grouping, never an edit. Exactly ONE producer-aware source resolver `resolveMeshUVs` feeds BOTH the panel AND the `__basher_uv_islands` seam (no drift, [[H40]]). `EvaluatedMesh.uvs` is populated EAGERLY only for the SYNC-available producers (box/sphere ‚Äî `geometryRegistry.get` builds from params); glTF/GltfChild/BakedMesh keep `uvs: null` in the pure resolver (their geometry is ASYNC ‚Äî asset clone / OPFS ‚Äî outside `resolveEvaluatedMesh`) and are resolved by `resolveMeshUVs` itself via the SAME extractor. Large meshes are stride-sampled to a face cap (`sampled` flag ‚Äî no silent truncation).

**Why it matters:** three traps. (1) Putting UV extraction in N surfaces (panel draws one set, a tool computes another) is the [[H40]] render‚âÝread class ‚Äî the ONE extractor + ONE `resolveMeshUVs` is the guard. (2) Computing UV islands EAGERLY inside `resolveEvaluatedMesh` for glTF would either force the pure sync resolver to touch async geometry (breaks [[V29]] purity) or pay island-extraction cost on every `dispatchApplyTransform`/boot-seam call that doesn't need UVs ‚Äî so only the cheap sync producers populate `uvs`, and the panel owns the async path. (3) Treating "view the UVs" as a license to EDIT them (write-back, seam moves) crosses the THESIS ¬ß58 domain boundary into Blender's territory; this invariant pins the editor as strictly read-only. Type: STRUCTURAL.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (v0.6 #3, issue #181, 2026-06-07). `src/app/uvIslands.ts` (`extractUVIslands` union-find + `unionUVBounds`), `src/app/resolveMeshUVs.ts` (the one producer-aware source), `src/app/resolveEvaluatedMesh.ts` (box/sphere eager `uvs`), `src/app/UVEditor.tsx` (real islands, retry-while-loading), `src/app/boot.ts` (`__basher_uv_islands` side-B seam). **Enforcement:** `src/app/uvIslands.test.ts` (BoxGeometry ‚Üí 6 islands each [0,0,1,1]; Sphere ‚Üí 1; non-indexed ‚Üí per-tri; no-uv ‚Üí empty; oversized ‚Üí sampled). **Observed live** (Lokayata, [[H40]]): `tests/e2e/p06-3-uv-display.spec.ts` (box 6 islands [0,0,1,1] ‚Äî the synthetic cross unfold could NOT pass; sphere 1; glTF child real loaded geometry). Cross-refs [[V29]] (the EvaluatedMesh face this fills ‚Äî `uvs` was reserved "populated by #3"), [[H40]] (panel == seam == real geometry), [[V32]] (the material/UV arc), dharana [[B19]]. REF: `.planning/phases/v06.3-uv-texture-placement/{CONTEXT,PLAN}.md` (A-1..A-4); commit `8db0774`; THESIS ¬ß58.

## V34 ‚Äî Every creative datum reduces to the ONE substrate (DAG ¬∑ Op ¬∑ serializable IR); no authoritative state outside it, no second pipeline ‚Äî and the north-star superlinearity holds ONLY as far as this holds

**Statement:** every datum a director or agent can create / edit / animate / render / composite is, by construction, a node/param/Op on the one DAG, evaluated to a value, persisted in the one serializable IR. There is **NO authoritative state outside the IR**, **NO mutation path that bypasses Ops** (¬ß18, ¬ß50), and **NO second graph / undo / renderer / UI** for any domain. The renderer/paint/solver engine is reached ONLY through a single adapter ([[V32]]). A **stochastic / generative output** (AI image / motion / mesh) is made an IR-citizen by **PINNING (seed) + CONTENT-HASHING its result as an asset** (the [[V30]] pattern) ‚Äî the model is not reproducible, the graph is. The **Op vocabulary stays small + coherent** (a new domain reuses Ops, never mints a parallel set). **"Advanced" controls are the SAME projected graph revealed** (projection engine ¬ß59a + progressive disclosure ¬ß17a), never a bolted-on second UI.

**Scope / faces:** the GENERALIZATION whose faces are already invariants ‚Äî [[V20]] (one writer), [[V29]] (one producer/resolver), [[V30]] (authoritative bytes persist, content-hashed), [[V32]] (renderer = compile target via one adapter), [[V33]] (UV = read-only projection), ¬ß18 (no agent-private path), ¬ß48‚Äì51 (determinism + serializable IR). V34 NAMES them as one rule and ADDS the leak-classes not yet covered: (a) stochastic-AI pinning, (b) Op-vocabulary bound, (c) no-second-UI-for-advanced, (d) no-state-outside-IR for any FUTURE domain (paint, composite, sim). **Breaks when:** an expedient shortcut stores domain state in a side-channel, references a live stochastic call as deterministic, ships a bespoke "advanced" panel, or balloons the Op set. Type: STRUCTURAL (the platform thesis).

**Why it matters:** the north-star superlinearity (`docs/PLATFORM-VISION.md` ¬ß9.3 ‚Äî N√óN integration-tax ‚Üí N√ó1) holds **ONLY while the substrate stays pure.** Each leak silently downgrades a multiplication back to an addition for everything that touches the leaked domain ‚Äî undo / replay / multiplayer / agent-authoring / the data-flywheel all stop spanning it. **Refusing leaks IS the moat** (¬ß9.4). Early leak tell already present: the bespoke `MATERIAL_LOBES` inspector sections (code where there should be projected data ‚Äî the L2-too-thin signal, [[H77]] detection #5).

**Status:** PARTIALLY ENFORCED / TARGET. The transform / material / UV / geometry faces are IMPLEMENTED ([[V20]]/[[V29]]/[[V30]]/[[V32]]/[[V33]]). NOT YET ENFORCED (forward guards ‚Äî no code yet): stochastic-AI pinning (no generative node domain pre-v0.7), Op-vocabulary bound (no metric/gate), no-second-UI (the v0.6 #4 chrome + v0.7 projection engine must hold it). Enforcement today = the dharana leak-check [[B-substrate-purity]] + this invariant + the [[H77]] pattern, NOT a test gate.

**REF:** `docs/PLATFORM-VISION.md` ¬ß9 (north star) + ¬ß9.4 (the one condition); THESIS ¬ß59a (projection engine + L2.5 interaction-as-composition) / ¬ß59b / ¬ß50 (Op = only mutation path) / ¬ß48‚Äì51 (determinism) / ¬ß18 (agent = privileged user) / ¬ß17a (progressive disclosure). Faces [[V20]] [[V29]] [[V30]] [[V32]] [[V33]] [[H76]]; leak pattern [[H77]]; dharana [[B-substrate-purity]].

## V35 ‚Äî A revealable / progressive-disclosure surface must keep its REVEAL affordance reachable while collapsed: gate the BODY on the open flag, NOT the affordance's container ‚Äî the container stays mounted/visible (collapse the body height to 0), so the toggle that re-opens it is never hidden behind the closed state it controls

**Statement:** for any surface that hides-by-default and reveals on demand (the timeline drawer, a future DAG view, the library, advanced inspector sections ‚Äî ¬ß17a progressive disclosure, the V34 "advanced = same graph revealed" face), the control that REVEALS it must NOT live inside the region that the closed state removes from view. Structurally: mount the slot/region ALWAYS; render the always-visible toggle bar unconditionally; gate only the BODY on the open flag (`{open && <body/>}` or a height/`display` collapse of the body alone). A "hide the whole region when closed" gate (`display:none` on the slot, or a mode that 0-widths it) STRANDS the reveal ‚Äî there is no surviving affordance to re-open, exactly when the user needs it. This is the structural sibling of [[H75]] (a control hidden by the very condition it would reset).

**Scope:** every hidden-by-default revealable surface. Today: the timeline drawer (`Layout.tsx` timeline slot ALWAYS `display:block`; `TimelineDrawer` renders the toggle bar outside `{open && ‚Ä¶}`, the body gated by `timelineDrawerOpen`). Forward: any v0.7 disclosure surface (raw-DAG view, node library, debug panels) ‚Äî they are the SAME projected graph revealed (V34), and each must carry its own always-reachable reveal. **Breaks when:** a wave gates the whole region on the open/mode flag (the v0.6 #4 W2 ordering hazard ‚Äî the only reveal control lived inside the slot, so `display:none` on the closed slot made the timeline unreachable for the entire W2‚ÜíW1 interval; MUST-FIX #3). Type: STRUCTURAL (disclosure-UX).

**Trade-off it forces (observe, don't infer):** keeping the toggle bar always-visible costs layout space even when collapsed (the v0.6 #4 timeline bar shrinks the viewport ~39px). The two resolutions: (a) accept the always-on bar (lowest churn ‚Äî W2 chose this); (b) move the reveal to a SIBLING always-visible surface (a toolbar button) and then the region itself can fully `display:none` when closed (no space cost). (b) is the cleaner end state once a consolidated toolbar exists to host the reveal ‚Äî v0.6 #4 W1 consolidates the floating pill and can adopt (b), letting the timeline slot collapse fully. The invariant holds under BOTH: the reveal must survive the collapse; WHERE the reveal lives (in-slot bar vs sibling toolbar) is the UX call.

**Status:** ENFORCED for the timeline drawer (v0.6 #4 W2). Forward guard for future disclosure surfaces (no test gate ‚Äî structural review at each new revealable surface).

**REF:** `src/app/Layout.tsx` (timeline slot always-mounted) + `src/timeline/TimelineDrawer.tsx` (toggle bar outside `{open}`, body gated on `timelineDrawerOpen`); THESIS ¬ß17a (progressive disclosure); [[V34]] face (c) (advanced = same graph revealed); sibling [[H75]] (control hidden by its own precondition); v0.6 #4 W2 MUST-FIX #3 (`.planning/phases/v06.4-director-ux/PLAN-CHECK.md`); W2 commit `b5af221`.

## V36 ‚Äî A semantic-hue token must clear AA-as-TEXT (4.5:1) AND SC 1.4.11-as-BORDER (3:1) on EVERY surface polarity it renders on; a hue tuned for one background polarity does NOT survive inversion in its text/border roles ‚Äî darken the TOKEN (preserve the hue family), do not split fill-vs-line across call-sites

**The invariant:** a hue that carries meaning (accent/warn/error/record) is used in three roles ‚Äî FILL (`bg-*`, large colored shape, knockout text on it), TEXT (`text-*`), and BORDER (`border-*` / focus ring, SC 1.4.11 3:1). A neon hue tuned for a DARK background (high luminance, e.g. accent `#5af07a` L‚âà0.66) works as a fill + as text/border on dark, but on a LIGHT surface it lands ~1.2‚Äì1.5:1 as text/border ‚Äî invisible. The fill role can keep a light hue (with dark knockout text), but the TEXT and BORDER roles require the hue to be dark enough for the surface.

**Why darken the token, not split roles:** splitting "neon for fills, dark variant for text/border" means touching every text-/border-/ring- call site (for the accent in this codebase: ~80 sites across 15 files ‚Äî the accent IS the universal focus-ring color). Darkening the single token to an AA-passing value in the SAME hue family fixes all roles at once with ZERO call-site changes, because the fill's knockout text (`text-bg`) auto-inverts correctly when the neutral `bg` token also inverts (light bg ‚Üí light knockout text on the now-dark fill). One token edit > 80 site edits, and "calmer" is usually the design intent on inversion anyway.

**Corollary (the inversion re-grounding, [[H27]] instance):** inverting a fg/bg relationship inverts EVERY worst-case assumption baked into the contrast gates ‚Äî the over-canvas composite backdrop flips (white‚Üíblack: a translucent LIGHT overlay is darkened, not lightened, by the scene behind it), the pixel-sampled "glyph" flips from the brightest to the darkest grayish pixel, and the falsification thresholds flip direction. Re-ground every gate that encoded the old polarity in the SAME wave (else it tests the wrong worst case and passes vacuously ‚Äî the dark-backdrop re-grounding immediately caught a real 4.48:1 the white version masked).

**Status:** ENFORCED, and the inversion is now confirmed **BIDIRECTIONAL and recurring** ‚Äî W3 inverted dark‚Üílight (calm LIGHT), then the Spline-exact redesign **Wave A** (commit `38c925c`) inverted it RIGHT BACK light‚Üídark. The SAME re-grounding ran in reverse: TOKEN mirror flipped, F7 page-bg literal `#ececf2`‚Üí`#0e0e11`, the `#57` over-canvas worst-case flipped DARK-backdrop‚ÜíBRIGHT-backdrop (dark chrome now paints LIGHT glyphs on a dark translucent surface ‚Üí a white/studio scene is the worst case), the p57 glyph-pick flipped darkest‚Üíbrightest grayish. **Wave A's "tune the token, don't split roles" instance:** the Spline accent BLUE landed 3.3‚Äì4.3:1 as accent-text on the accent-TINTED active fills; brightening the single token `#3b82f6`‚Üí`#5c9dff` cleared all of them at once (vs splitting per call-site) ‚Äî the contrast matrix VERBOSE drove the iteration (7 fails‚Üí2‚Üí0). TWO inversions in two waves promotes V36 from "an invariant" to "the re-grounding is a routine, two-directional operation ‚Äî every palette polarity flip re-runs the SAME gate-flips in the SAME wave." GROUNDED by observation each time (matrix failed until tokens cleared; W3 dark-backdrop caught a real 4.48:1; Wave A's pixel-sample exposed [[H83]]).

**REF:** `tailwind.config.ts` (semantic tokens ‚Äî DARK as of Wave A: accent `#5c9dff`), `src/a11y/contrastMatrix.test.ts` (TOKEN mirror + F2 drift gate + border-token-gate 3:1 + the re-grounded #57 ‚Äî now BRIGHT-backdrop `it()` + F7 literal `#0e0e11`), `tests/e2e/p57-bright-scene-contrast.spec.ts` (re-grounded worst-case BRIGHT + glyph-pick brightest + falsification + [[H83]] solid-sub-element sample), `src/viewport/viewportColors.ts` (dark canvas, named); CONTEXT D-07 (W3 light) + Spline-redesign Wave A (dark); commits `29a3afe` (W3 light), `38c925c` (Wave A dark). Sibling [[V34]]/[[V35]]; [[H27]] (re-validation trap); [[H83]] (the Wave A pixel-sample degeneration).

## V37 ‚Äî Every editor-only viewport object carries `userData.editorChrome === true`; an image render shows DAG content ONLY (chrome is excluded by the render's hide-pass)

<!-- Renumbered V32‚ÜíV37 on the ux-overhall integration: the camera/render/notify
     lineage independently assigned V32/V33 while the material lineage took the
     same numbers (parallel-branch collision, H79). editorChrome = V37, surface-
     outcome = V38. Cross-references to [[V32]]/[[V33]] meaning these two now
     point to V37/V38. -->

**Statement:** anything mounted in the viewport scene graph that is NOT DAG-evaluated content ‚Äî the floor grid, the transform gizmo, the camera/light wireframe helpers, the editor fill-light rig (`EditorLights`), the walk-to ground plane, the agent-diff ghost overlay ‚Äî MUST carry `userData.editorChrome === true` on its root object (or be a `three.js` `TransformControls*`-typed object, caught by type since the drei gizmo can't carry the flag). The #168 image render (`renderToImage.renderSceneToPngBlob`) traverses the live scene and hides every such object (saving + restoring `.visible` in a `finally`) before rendering offscreen, so a render is "what production sees" ‚Äî DAG meshes + DAG lights only. The denylist is deliberately chosen over an allowlist: a missed chrome mark LEAKS a visible, catchable artifact (a grid line), whereas a missed content mark would make a user's object silently VANISH from their render ‚Äî the catastrophic direction.

**Why it matters:** without this invariant, the next editor-only scene object added (a new helper, a bounding-box overlay, a snapping guide, a VR controller model) leaks into every render with no error ‚Äî the render just silently shows editor furniture the director never authored. The flag is the single, greppable contract that keeps "the editor view" and "the production render" separable while they share ONE live scene graph (Basher does NOT maintain a parallel render scene ‚Äî the dhyana "do not invent a parallel walk" discipline). EditorLights is the sharpest case: it's invisible _geometry_ but it changes the _lighting_ ‚Äî unflagged, a render is over-lit by the studio fill, not the DAG lights, and the error is a plausible-looking brighter image, not a crash.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#168, 2026-06-05). Marks: `src/viewport/Viewport.tsx` (Grid wrapper group), `src/viewport/EditorLights.tsx` (fill-rig group), `src/viewport/CameraHelpers.tsx` + `src/viewport/LightHelpers.tsx` (helper root groups), `src/app/character/GroundClick.tsx` (merged into existing userData), `src/viewport/DiffOverlay.tsx` (ghost root). Hide-pass + TransformControls type-catch: `src/render/renderToImage.ts`.

**Enforcement:** `tests/e2e/p168-render-to-image.spec.ts` ‚Äî the cube-free bottom-left quadrant of the render is pure background when chrome is excluded; PHYSICALLY FALSIFIED during Wave D (disable the hide-pass ‚Üí the floor grid leaks 221 non-bg pixels into that quadrant ‚Üí the test fails; enabled ‚Üí 0). Cross-ref [[H68]] (the offscreen-render parent ‚Äî chrome exclusion is one of its four correctness axes), dharana [[B17]]. REF: issue #168; `src/render/renderToImage.ts` (the `userData.editorChrome === true || o.type.startsWith('TransformControls')` denylist), the mark sites above.

## V38 ‚Äî Every user-triggered fallible or degradable action surfaces its outcome ‚Äî no silent no-op

**Statement:** an action a user can invoke that may FAIL (returns `{ ok: false, ‚Ä¶ }`, throws-and-is-caught, produces nothing) or silently DEGRADE (selects a fallback capability/path) MUST surface that outcome to the user through the notification surface (`notificationStore` ‚Üí `ToastViewport`): success ‚Üí a confirmation, failure ‚Üí an error toast carrying a reason, degradation ‚Üí a (sticky) warning. Representing the outcome as a return value or an internal branch is necessary but NOT sufficient ‚Äî a caller that `void`s the result, or a fallback site with no notification, violates this invariant. The outcome‚Üítoast mapping is a PURE function (`renderResultToToast`, `storageFallbackWarning`) so it is unit-testable without the live operation, and the action's core return value is preserved for callers that still need it.

**Why it matters:** the silent no-op is invisible by construction ‚Äî no throw means no console error, and a discarded result means nothing reaches the UI. The user experiences "I clicked and nothing happened" or "I reloaded and my work was gone," with no diagnostic. As Basher grows fallible actions (render, export, publish, capability probes, future Tauri-fs), each one that skips this invariant re-creates a silent-failure class that looks handled (the outcome IS represented) but isn't surfaced ([[H70]]).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED for the first two callers (#170 render, #148 storage), 2026-06-05; **both issues CLOSED 2026-06-16** (`ux-overhall` `a00ba75`). Surface: `src/app/stores/notificationStore.ts` + `src/app/ToastViewport.tsx` (App-root mount). Callers: `src/app/renderImageAction.ts` (`renderImageWithFeedback` consumes the render result), `src/app/boot.ts` (boot consumes `storageFallbackWarning(storage.kind)`). The render outcome now has TWO entry points that both consume it ‚Äî the File menu (`MenuBar`) AND a `top-toolbar-render` button (`FloatingViewportToolbar`, added `a00ba75` with a "Rendering‚Ä¶" disabled affordance for slow large renders). Note: the _wiring_ (V38) was done 2026-06-05 but the toolbar lacked the button, so the existing `notify-surface` spec was red until the entry point landed ‚Äî the invariant held at the action layer while a surface to invoke it was missing (a reminder that V38 needs both the consume-the-outcome wiring AND a reachable trigger). NOT YET enforced for: future fallible actions (export/publish/Tauri-fs) ‚Äî each new one MUST wire its outcome into the surface.

**Enforcement:** `tests/e2e/notify-surface.spec.ts` ‚Äî success toast on render, sticky warn toast on Memory-fallback boot; both PHYSICALLY FALSIFIED (disable the notify wiring ‚Üí no toast ‚Üí fails). Unit: `renderImageAction.test.ts` + `storageFallbackWarning.test.ts` (pure mappers, both branches). Detection for new violations: grep `void .*Action(` for discarded results + capability fallback sites without an adjacent notify. Cross-ref [[H70]] (the silent-no-op pattern this invariant forbids), assetErrorStore (persistent-error sibling), dharana [[B18]]. REF: issues #170, #148.

## V39 ‚Äî Every full-viewport surface in the dark redesign renders TRANSPARENT over the body's fixed ambient stage; the glow is defined ONCE (`body`, index.css) and reused, never re-painted per surface

**Statement:** the Spline-dark ambient glow (corner blooms over `#0e0e11`) is painted exactly once, on `body` (`src/index.css`, `background-attachment: fixed`). Every full-viewport chrome surface ‚Äî the editor `Layout`, the `Home` launcher, and any future full-page route (settings, publish, a gallery) ‚Äî MUST render transparent (no opaque page-level background token) so that one glow reads through as a shared lit stage. Panels mounted ON a surface stay translucent (`bg-2/90`, `bg/95`, etc.) so the glow reads through them too (the "floating panel on a lit stage" look). A surface that paints an opaque page-level bg (`bg-bg`) occludes the stage and forks the treatment ‚Äî forbidden ([[H85]]). Corollary (token discipline): a new chrome surface reuses the editor's ALREADY-AUDITED token vocabulary (the translucent panel opacities `bg-2/90`/`bg/95`, `bg-1`, `bg-muted`, `bg-accent/15`) ‚Äî this both holds the visual language AND keeps the unit `contrastMatrix.test.ts` coverage gate green without new ROWS (the gate fires on any new `text-/bg-/border-` token class, INCLUDING token-shaped strings in comments).

**Why it matters:** without this invariant, each new full-page surface independently chooses a background and either (a) goes opaque ‚Üí disconnects from the stage and gets "fixed" by a drifting second glow ([[H85]]), or (b) invents new translucent token variants ‚Üí trips the contrast gate and tempts whitelist-bloat. The invariant collapses both: be transparent, reuse audited tokens. As the redesign adds surfaces (Waves remaining + post-v0.6 routes), this is the single rule that keeps them on one stage with one token vocabulary.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED for Home (Wave E, 2026-06-10) and the editor Layout (Waves A‚ÄìC). Surface roots: `src/app/Home.tsx` (transparent), `src/app/Layout.tsx` (editor shell), glow source `src/index.css` (`body`). NOT YET enforced for: future full-page routes ‚Äî each new one MUST be transparent + reuse audited tokens.

**Enforcement:** `tests/e2e/spline-we-home.spec.ts` ‚Äî the Home root computed `backgroundColor === 'rgba(0, 0, 0, 0)'` (transparent ‚Üí glow reads through); PHYSICALLY FALSIFIED (re-add `bg-bg` ‚Üí `rgb(14, 14, 17)` ‚Üí fails). Token reuse is enforced by the existing `src/a11y/contrastMatrix.test.ts` coverage+border gates (a new token class ‚Üí gate fail ‚Üí reuse-or-classify). Cross-ref [[H85]] (the occlusion bug this forbids), [[V34]] (one substrate/treatment reused), dharana [[B20]]. REF: `src/index.css`, `src/app/Home.tsx`, `src/app/Layout.tsx`. Branch `ux-overhall`.

## V40 ‚Äî A scroll panel scrolls ONLY when its whole ancestor chain to the bounded track sets `min-height:0`; chrome panels overflow-scroll INTERNALLY (bounded), and hide the native scrollbar via the ONE `.no-scrollbar` utility ‚Äî verified by injecting content, not by clamping the container

**Statement:** every overflow-scroll chrome panel (the outliner `SceneTree`, the inspector `NPanel`, and any future paneled grid/flex region) MUST (a) keep `overflow-y-auto` on the scroll root AND (b) have `min-height:0` on EVERY ancestor between that root and the height-bounded track ‚Äî most importantly the CSS-grid cell wrapper and any in-cell flex column. Without (b), a grid/flex item's auto minimum (`min-content`) lets the panel grow to its content and, in a shared `1fr` row, drags the whole row past the viewport ‚Äî so the panel never overflows and never scrolls ([[H86]]). The bar is hidden cross-browser by the single `.no-scrollbar` utility (`src/index.css` `@layer utilities`: `scrollbar-width:none` + `::-webkit-scrollbar{display:none}` + `-ms-overflow-style:none`) applied to the scroll root ‚Äî NOT by per-component CSS, and NOT relied upon for layout (it only hides the bar; bounding is (b)'s job).

**Why it matters:** "the panel won't scroll" is one of the easiest bugs to ship green, because the two obvious checks are INERT: clamping the container's height proves the CSS can scroll but not that the layout bounds it, and a scrollbar-gutter check is inert on overlay-scrollbar platforms (macOS/headless Chromium reserve no gutter either way). This invariant fixes the contract (bounded chain) AND the way to prove it (inject content + assert `clientHeight ‚â™ scrollHeight` + `scrollTop` moves + `body.scrollHeight ‚â§ viewport`; assert computed `scrollbar-width === 'none'` for the hidden bar). As the redesign adds panels, this is the single rule that keeps them scrollable-but-bar-less.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED for the outliner + inspector (2026-06-11). Scroll roots: `src/app/SceneTree.tsx` (`overflow-y-auto no-scrollbar`), `src/app/NPanel.tsx` (`overflow-y-auto no-scrollbar`); bounding chain: `src/app/Layout.tsx` inspector grid-cell `minHeight:0`, `src/app/LeftSidebar.tsx` aside `min-h-0`; utility: `src/index.css`. NOT YET enforced for: future paneled regions ‚Äî each MUST set the `min-height:0` chain + reuse `.no-scrollbar`.

**Enforcement:** `tests/e2e/spline-panel-scroll.spec.ts` ‚Äî injects a 2000px child into each panel and asserts `overflowY==='auto'`, `clientHeight ‚â™ scrollHeight`, `scrollTop > 0`, `body.scrollHeight ‚â§ viewport`, and computed `scrollbar-width === 'none'`. PHYSICALLY FALSIFIED both ways: removing `minHeight:0` blows the page out (bounded-assertion red); removing `.no-scrollbar` flips `scrollbar-width` to `auto` (bar-assertion red). Cross-ref [[H86]] (the bug this forbids), dharana [[B20]] (inert-falsifier discipline). REF: `src/app/{Layout,LeftSidebar,SceneTree,NPanel}.tsx`, `src/index.css`, `tests/e2e/spline-panel-scroll.spec.ts`. Commits `791de2a` + `3792699`. Branch `ux-overhall`.

---

### V41 ‚Äî A self-contained `.basher` scene file embeds the COMPLETE OPFS-backed reference span; the collector is SHAPE-driven (not per-node-type), so a new ref shape is captured automatically

**Invariant:** the native scene file (`.basher`) is the DAG state PLUS every OPFS-backed asset it references, embedded as base64, so it opens identically on any machine. "Every asset it references" is a complete span ‚Äî drop one and the file is a silently-broken portable (it renders blank/errors on a machine that lacks that asset). The three OPFS-backed reference shapes as of v0.6 are: (1) `GltfAsset.assetRef` strings under `user-imports/<folder>/` (embed the WHOLE folder ‚Äî multi-file glTF siblings); (2) baked `GeometryDescriptor {kind:'baked',hash,vertexCount}` ‚Üí `baked-geometry/<hash>-<vc>.bin`; (3) `BakedTextureRef {hash,colorSpace,flipY,‚Ä¶}` ‚Üí `baked-texture/<hash>.<ext>` (BakedMesh material maps AND primitive/material `maps.*`). App-shipped `assets/‚Ä¶` (seedOpfs) are EXCLUDED ‚Äî they are re-seeded on every instance, so embedding them is dead weight + a privacy leak.

**Why it matters:** the baked-\* and user-imports stores are GLOBAL, content-addressed, shared across ALL projects ‚Äî so the file must embed PRECISELY what THIS DAG references, never the whole store (that would leak other projects' assets into a shared file). And the reference span grows: any new node type or feature that carries an OPFS handle silently widens it. A per-node-type collector would drop the new shape (an [[H77]] substrate leak: works in isolation, breaks on share/replay). The guard is a SHAPE-driven recursive param walk ‚Äî it captures any value matching one of the three handle shapes wherever it nests, regardless of which node owns it ‚Äî so a future handle-bearing node is embedded automatically.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED 2026-06-11 (`ux-overhall`). `src/app/sceneBundle.ts` (`collectAssetRefs` shape-walk + `resolveAssetFiles` + base64 + `bundleToProject` = loadProject's exact ladder); `src/app/boot.ts` (`buildSceneBundleForCurrent` embed + `importSceneBundle` rehydrate-write-if-absent ‚Üí new-project hydrate); `src/app/sceneFileActions.ts` + MenuBar (Save/Open affordances). Open semantics = NEW project (non-destructive). NOT YET: a 4th handle shape (e.g. an OPFS-backed video/cache node) MUST either match one of the three detector shapes or extend the walk.

**Enforcement:** `src/app/sceneBundle.test.ts` (15 unit: each ref shape + nesting + `assets/` exclusion + base64 round-trip + load-ladder). `tests/e2e/menu-scene-file.spec.ts` ‚Äî export‚Üídiverge‚Üíopen round-trip (node id-set survives), non-destructive new-project, and the end-to-end portability falsifier: ingest glTF ‚Üí export embeds the bytes ‚Üí DELETE the OPFS asset ‚Üí open ‚Üí assert the bytes are rehydrated back. BOTH directions physically falsified (revert hydrate ‚Üí DAG test red; revert the rehydrate write-loop ‚Üí asset test red). Cross-ref [[H77]] (the leak this forbids), [[V34]] (one substrate), [[H87]] (the same-scene round-trip inert falsifier), dharana [[B21]]. REF: `src/app/{sceneBundle,sceneFileActions,boot}.ts`, `src/app/MenuBar.tsx`, `src/app/exportDag.ts` (the legacy DAG-only emitter this is symmetric to), `tests/e2e/menu-scene-file.spec.ts`. Branch `ux-overhall`.

## V42 ‚Äî A render component subscribes to the NARROWEST DAG slice it consumes, not the whole node table; under structural sharing, subscribe to its dependency-node REFS with `shallow`, so an unrelated edit is shallow-equal and does not re-render

**The invariant:** a React renderer that reads DAG state must subscribe to the smallest slice whose change actually alters its output. A `useSyncExternalStore` subscription (zustand) fires INDEPENDENTLY of whether the memoized parent skipped ‚Äî so `useDagStore((s) => s.state.nodes)` re-renders the component on EVERY dispatch (the whole `nodes` ref flips per edit, `ops.ts:278-282` structural sharing). The correct form selects only the dependency nodes and compares with `shallow` (`useStoreWithEqualityFn`): structural sharing keeps every unchanged node's ref identical, so an unrelated edit yields a shallow-EQUAL selection ‚Üí no emit ‚Üí no re-render; a relevant edit flips exactly one element's ref ‚Üí re-render. Two memos that the cost lives behind (`childOverrides`, `bakedChannels`) then key on the narrowed selection, so the full-table walks vanish too.

**Why it matters:** this is the load-bearing half of the H48 "memoize per-node subtrees" lever. The `SceneChildNode` value-ref memo (52a3958) closes the PARENT re-render path, but a leaf that re-subscribes broadly re-opens it through its own subscription ‚Äî the memo cannot help a `useSyncExternalStore` re-render. On a ~700-node import that single broad subscription IS the "edit anything ‚Üí the imported model re-renders at ~16fps" cost ([[H48]] 4th/5th occ). It generalises: any future per-asset / per-region renderer that needs live DAG reads (a scatter system, a per-instance material layer) must scope its subscription the same way or it reintroduces the cost.

**The trap it forbids:** subscribing to `s.state` or `s.state.nodes` "to be safe," then deriving inside a `useMemo`. The memo recompute is cheap, but the SUBSCRIPTION already re-rendered the component ‚Äî the memo runs AFTER React decided to re-render. The granularity must be at the subscription (equality fn), not the derivation.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED 2026-06-11 (`02f04a1`, `ux-overhall`) for `GltfAssetR`. NOT YET applied to other live-DAG-reading leaves (none currently subscribe broadly ‚Äî `GltfAssetR` was the only one, grep `useDagStore` in `src/viewport/`). A future broad subscriber is the next occurrence.

**Enforcement:** `tests/e2e/perf-render-count.spec.ts` (DEV `bumpRenderCount` seam ‚Üí edit a sibling 10√ó ‚Üí asset re-renders +0; own-node edit +1) + `src/app/gltfAssetDeps.test.ts` (unrelated edit ‚Üí `shallow`-equal dep array; relevant edit ‚Üí different). Falsified: a broad `Object.values(s.state.nodes)` selector turns the +0 into +10 (observed). Cross-ref [[H48]] (the cost class), [[H40]] (the freeze guard the relevant-edit re-render preserves), [[V8]] (no store WRITES in render ‚Äî V42 is its read-side sibling: narrowest READ), dharana [[B13]]. REF: `src/app/gltfAssetDeps.ts`, `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` GltfAssetR, `src/perf/renderCounter.ts`, `src/core/dag/ops.ts:278-282`. Branch `ux-overhall`.

## V43 ‚Äî Per-node `evaluate` cost is O(changed), not O(scene): `hashValue(node.params)` is memoized by the params OBJECT identity, sound ONLY because `setParam` replaces params and structural sharing keeps unchanged nodes' params by reference

**The invariant:** the dominant cost of `evaluate` is `hashValue(node.params)` (the cache KEY is built BEFORE the cache lookup ‚Äî evaluator.ts:127 ‚Äî so a warm cache cannot avoid it). For a heavy import (a glTF TransformClip with hundreds of per-bone tracks) that single node's hash measured ~35ms, recomputed on EVERY uncached evaluate. The evaluator memoizes it in a module-level `WeakMap<object, ContentHash>` keyed by the params object identity. This is EXACT ‚Äî not a content guess ‚Äî because of the DAG's write discipline: `applySetParam` (`ops.ts:264-289`) produces a FRESH `parsed.data` for the edited node only, and structural sharing ([[V42]], `ops.ts:278-282`) leaves every unchanged node's params object identical by reference. So a WeakMap HIT means the params object is the same object ‚áí byte-identical content ‚áí the cached hash is valid; a changed param is a NEW object ‚áí miss ‚áí recompute that one node. Per-node param hashing is therefore O(changed), not O(scene).

**Why it matters:** this is the actual lever behind the cicada edit-lag ([[H48]] 7th occ) ‚Äî the read-side resolvers (`resolveEvaluatedTransform`/`resolveTransformParam`) evaluate UNCACHED, repeatedly, per inspector transform row, so the heavy-asset param hash was paid ~3-6√ó/commit (~458ms/frame). With the memo, evaluation drops to O(changed): edit-lag 590‚Üí14ms, AND the general per-edit React reconcile (the scene re-render that evaluates during render) 44‚Üí8ms. It generalises beyond glTF: ANY node whose params grow large (a procedural field, a large keyframe table, a big material graph) is covered automatically ‚Äî the cost is bounded by what CHANGED, regardless of params size of unchanged nodes.

**The trap it forbids:** "fix the slow evaluate by passing a shared `EvaluatorCache`." Measured DEAD (warm 34.2ms ‚âà uncached 35.7ms) ‚Äî the cache key requires the param hash, computed before the lookup, so caching the VALUE saves only the (trivial) `def.evaluate` body, not the hash. The fix must attack the HASH recomputation, not the value cache. Also forbidden: memoizing by the NODE object instead of the params object (a node could in principle be re-wrapped with the same params ‚Äî params identity is the finer, correct key) and mutating `node.params` in place (would make the memo stale ‚Äî the clone-on-write invariant is load-bearing for this memo's correctness).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED 2026-06-12 (`6fa544a`, `ux-overhall`) in `src/core/dag/evaluator.ts` (`hashParams` + `paramsHashMemo`). Depends on the structural-sharing invariant ([[V42]]) and the clone-on-write `setParam` ([[B13]]/ops.ts) staying true ‚Äî if a future Op ever mutates params in place, this memo breaks silently (stale hash ‚Üí wrong cache key ‚Üí stale render). That is the one thing to re-check before any change to `ops.ts` params handling.

**Enforcement:** `src/core/dag/paramsHashMemo.test.ts` ‚Äî (1) correctness: memoized eval hash stable across evaluates + distinct content yields distinct hash + value unaffected; (2) mechanism: a STABLE params ref re-evaluates ‚â•5√ó cheaper than a FRESH-but-equal ref each call (a regression that re-hashes unchanged params every evaluate fails it). Proven end-to-end on the real cicada (headed Firefox A/B, [[H48]] 7th occ): `resolveEvaluatedTransform` 69.4‚Üí0.5ms. Cross-ref [[H48]] (the cost class + the 3-session misdiagnosis), [[V42]] (the structural-sharing invariant this depends on), [[H49]] (the sibling "time in the value-shape" lever), dharana [[B13]]/B-gizmo. REF: `src/core/dag/evaluator.ts`, `src/core/dag/hash.ts`, `src/core/dag/ops.ts:264-289`. Commit `6fa544a`.

**CORRECTION (2026-06-12, [[H48]] 6th occ).** The invariant (subscribe to the narrowest slice) is SOUND as a principle, but its perf JUSTIFICATION was falsified. An end-to-end frame-budget A/B on the real cicada (headed Firefox) showed the subscription fix removes re-renders (59‚Üí0) but **does NOT move frame time** (churn 43.2ms old vs 43.8ms new). It removes genuinely wasted work (correctness/efficiency) but the cicada's edit-lag bottleneck was never GltfAssetR ‚Äî it is the GIZMO/selection path (~117ms gizmo-mounted + ~414ms editing a selected child) plus a ~34ms scene-subtree React reconcile per edit. So: keep V42 as a hygiene rule, do NOT cite it as the fix for "manipulate ‚Üí fps drop." Gate any subscription change with `perf-render-count.spec.ts` for the MECHANISM, but prove PERF only with a frame.mean A/B + a component microbench. See [[H48]] 6th occ.

## V44 ‚Äî A correspondence across the import-producer ‚Üî render-clone boundary must be keyed by a STABLE INDEX/id, never by a re-derived NAME ‚Äî the two sides sanitize and dedup names differently, so name-matching silently drops the divergent subset

**The invariant:** when Basher's import producer and three's GLTFLoader both derive a per-node key from the SAME glTF, they do NOT agree on the string. The producer (`buildNodeNameMap`) keys by `sanitizeBoneName(raw)` + `${base}__${n}` dedup, and assigns `node_${i}` to UNNAMED nodes. three's `createUniqueName` (GLTFLoader.js:3653) keys by `PropertyBinding.sanitizeNodeName(raw)` + `${base}_${n}` dedup, and leaves UNNAMED nodes as `''`. Different sanitizer, different dedup separator, and unnamed nodes that can NEVER match. So any producer‚Üîrenderer map keyed by name silently loses the divergent subset (~28% on the real cicada: 273/379). The one value both sides compute identically is the glTF node INDEX: the producer iterates `json.nodes` in index order; three records the index on `gltf.parser.associations` for EVERY loaded object, named or not (GLTFLoader.js:4311). Therefore the correspondence must travel as an index/id: persist `index ‚Üí key` at import (`keyByGltfNodeIndex`), and at render pair original‚Üîclone (SkeletonUtils preserves child order + deep-copies userData) to STAMP the resolved DAG id onto each clone object (`userData.basherGltfChildId`). Consumers then read the stamp, never re-derive the name.

**Why it matters:** the viewport drill-in ([[H90]]) matched `hitObject.name` against `nodeNameMap` and silently no-drilled on a real export. The SAME latent gap exists wherever a clone object must be addressed back to its DAG node by name: per-child TRS/material/suppress OVERRIDES in `GltfAssetR` (`nameToObject.get(key)`) silently no-op on the mismatched subset today ‚Äî same root cause, fixable by the same stamp. It generalises to every future producer‚Üîthree correspondence (animation tracks, material assignment, UV islands): the moment a name is RE-DERIVED on the far side of a sanitizing boundary, it is a guess, not an identity.

**The trap it forbids:** "stamp the id where the per-child overrides already iterate `nodeNameMap` keys" ‚Äî that stamps ONLY the already-matching subset (it reuses the failing `nameToObject.get(name)` lookup), so it fixes nothing for the divergent ~28%. The stamp must be driven by the INDEX correspondence (`associations` √ó `keyByGltfNodeIndex`), not by the name lookup it is meant to replace. Also forbidden: "reconcile the two sanitizers so the names match" ‚Äî that still cannot address UNNAMED nodes (both sides collapse them, three to `''`, so they remain unaddressable by name), and it would change the content-addressed childId (`hashId(assetRef, key)`) ‚Üí break saved projects.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED for drill 2026-06-14 (`c5f18fc`). `keyByGltfNodeIndex` persisted on `GltfAsset` (additive `.default({})`, no schema bump); `GltfAssetR` stamps the clone; `buildGltfDrillChain` reads stamps (name-match fallback for pre-2026-06-14 saves). EXTENDED 2026-06-14 (`54c249e`): the per-child TRS + suppression consumers in `GltfAssetR` now also resolve by stamped id via the shared `src/viewport/gltfChildObjects.ts` (`buildChildIdToObject`/`resolveChildObject`) ‚Äî closing the [[H90]] FOLLOW-UP (material overrides were slot-INDEX based, never by name, so unaffected). A THIRD consumer now reads the same stamp: the UX #8 read-only material readout (`readGltfMaterials` tags each render slot with its nearest stamped `basherGltfChildId` so the inspector can filter to a selected GltfChild, `d28542f`). The stamp is now the canonical clone‚ÜîDAG-node bridge for drill, overrides, suppression, and material inspection.

**Enforcement:** `src/viewport/gltfDrillChain.test.ts` (stamped-id path drills when names diverge from `nodeNameMap`; material-split `<unnamed>` leaf ‚Üí nearest stamped ancestor; stamp wins over name-match; fallback when unstamped) + `tests/e2e/ux7-drill-in-select.spec.ts` (asserts `keyByGltfNodeIndex` persisted + the rendered mesh carries `userData.basherGltfChildId` ‚Üí a real GltfChild). Observed on the real cicada: 0 orphans within the import (was ~28% by name). Cross-ref [[H90]] (the bug), [[H40]] (id-space ‚âÝ render-space, the sibling boundary-pair class), `buildNodeNameMap`/`gltfImportChain.ts`, GLTFLoader.js:3653/4311. REF: `src/viewport/gltfDrillChain.ts`, `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` (GltfAssetR stamp), `src/core/import/gltfImportChain.ts`, `src/nodes/GltfAsset.ts`. Commit `c5f18fc`.

## V45 ‚Äî A spawned overlay (menu / submenu / popover) computes its placement against the LIVE available viewport space, never a hardcoded side or an edge constant; ONE shared placement primitive serves every such surface so the rule can't hold in one menu and fail in another

**The invariant:** any panel that opens relative to a trigger ‚Äî a top-level dropdown, a hover submenu, a context menu ‚Äî must place itself by MEASURING where the trigger actually is and how much room remains, then choosing a position that keeps the whole panel on-screen. A hardcoded direction (`left-full`, `r.top`) or a one-sided clamp encodes a hidden assumption about where the chrome sits; the moment the chrome moves or the trigger lands near an edge, the panel renders over its own trigger or off the viewport (no error, just visually wrong ‚Äî the [[H91]] family). The placement logic lives in ONE primitive (`src/app/menu/useFlyoutSide.ts` for submenus; `toolbarMenuAnchor` for the toolbar menus) that every surface consumes, so a fix or a future relocation can't silently regress just one call site (the V34 "one home" face applied to chrome geometry).

**The non-obvious sub-rule (why flip-only is insufficient):** "flip the panel to the other side when this side overflows" is NOT enough on its own. A left-aligned menu bar sits near x=0, so a left-flip of a wide submenu falls off the LEFT edge just as the right-open fell off the right ‚Äî neither pure side fits. The placement must degrade: prefer the natural side ‚Üí flip to the other side if THAT fits ‚Üí else CLAMP the panel to the viewport edge (accept overlapping the parent). Pure flip handles a free-floating menu near the right edge (room on its left ‚Äî the Add menu); clamp is required for the bar that can't fit the submenu on either side (View ‚ñ∏ Shading at a narrow width). This was found by observation: the flip-only first cut passed the Add-menu test and FAILED the 640w MenuBar test.

**Breaks when:** a new menu surface hardcodes `left-full`/`right-full` or an absolute `top:`/`left:` px instead of consuming the shared primitive; a clamp is added on only one bound (`Math.min` without `Math.max(margin,‚Ä¶)`) so the near-top/near-left edge is unguarded; the primitive is forked per-surface (re-introducing the divergence V34 forbids). Type: STRUCTURAL (chrome-geometry / disclosure-UX). Sibling of [[V35]] (a revealable surface keeps its reveal reachable) and [[V39]] (one glow defined once, reused) ‚Äî all three are "one chrome rule, defined once, reused across every surface it governs".

**Enforcement:** `tests/e2e/ux5-menu-submenu-edge.spec.ts` (submenu stays within the viewport at a narrow width AND near the right edge; still opens rightward when there is room ‚Äî falsified by reverting to a hardcoded `left-full`) + `tests/e2e/ux5-toolbar-menu-position.spec.ts` (the toolbar Add menu opens below the pill, anchored to its live rect). Cross-ref [[H91]] (the placement-constant pattern this invariant forbids), [[V34]] (one substrate/treatment reused), dharana [[B11]] (chrome re-validation). REF: `src/app/menu/useFlyoutSide.ts`, `src/app/MenuBar.tsx` (`Submenu`, `onMenubarKeyDown`, `hoverSwitch`), `src/app/AddMenu.tsx` (`AddMenuGroup`), `src/app/FloatingViewportToolbar.tsx` (`toolbarMenuAnchor`). Commits `5fd98d1` (anchor), `4f5ead1` (flyout), `ee1f9ed` (behaviour). Branch `ux-overhall`.

## V46 ‚Äî Floating chrome islands over a full-bleed viewport share ONE geometry source; every surface floating over the viewport must reserve a clear region for the others ‚Äî with no grid to reserve space, OVERLAP is the default failure

**The invariant:** once the chrome panels stop being grid columns/rows and become absolute islands over a full-bleed viewport (UX-BACKLOG #2), the layout no longer reserves space for anyone ‚Äî a panel and a viewport widget can occupy the same pixels with no error, just visual collision. So: (1) all island geometry (gaps, panel widths, the reserved bottom-widget band, the centered-surface side reserve, the narrow breakpoint) lives in ONE module `src/app/layoutIslands.ts` ‚Äî never hardcoded per surface (the V34/V45 "one home" face). (2) Side islands are TOP-anchored and stop short of the bottom (`BOTTOM_BAND`) so the already-floating bottom-right orbit gizmo + Persp/Ortho and the bottom-center stack stay clear ‚Äî the lowest-coupling fix (no widget dodges a panel). (3) Any VIEWPORT-CENTERED surface (the toolbar pill, the agent/timeline stack) caps its width so it can't slide under a side island ‚Äî and that reserve is **collapse-AWARE** (`centerSideReserved(leftCollapsed, inspectorCollapsed)`, follow-up 1): folding a side panel to its 28px strip frees the centered surface to reclaim that width, instead of reserving for the expanded footprint it no longer has (a STATIC reserve leaves the toolbar/stack needlessly narrow when both panels are folded). (4) An island that overlaps `<main>` stops `onContextMenu` propagation so a panel right-click doesn't pop the viewport Add menu. (5) **Responsive floor (follow-up 2):** below `LAYOUT_NARROW_MAX` (1024px) three columns of chrome can't fit, so the layout RE-DOCKS ‚Äî side panels become off-canvas overlay drawers (closed by default, an edge tab reveals one, a scrim dismisses it; ephemeral non-persisted `narrowLeft/RightDrawerOpen`), the toolbar + bottom stack go full-width, and the bottom-right orbit gizmo + Persp/Ortho are hidden (no clear corner survives full-width). The breakpoint is read through ONE guarded `useIsNarrowLayout()` hook; every narrow branch guards on `isNarrow` so the desktop layout renders byte-identically. (6) **Bounded center surface (the 2D View, `59fccec`):** a centered surface that is NOT the topmost chrome ‚Äî it sits in the toolbar's horizontal band ‚Äî must ALSO drop below the toolbar (`CENTER_SURFACE_TOP`) and stop above the bottom stack (`BOTTOM_BAND`), not just cap its side width. A top-anchored centered surface (full-bleed `inset:0`) slides its tabs/headers UNDER the floating toolbar AND the side islands (observed: the 2D View's UV/Render-Result tabs rendered behind the outliner island until it became a bounded box). So the 2D View is a bounded center island: `top:CENTER_SURFACE_TOP, bottom:BOTTOM_BAND`, centered with the same collapse-aware `centerSideReserved` width (no 960 cap ‚Äî the editor fills the band), `display:block` preserved for the p26 contract. See [[V80]].

**Breaks when:** a new floating panel hardcodes its own width/offset instead of consuming `layoutIslands.ts` ‚Üí it drifts from the others when one changes; a centered surface omits the reserve cap ‚Üí it slides under a side island at narrow widths (observed: the toolbar's right end disappeared under the inspector at 1100px before the cap); the reserve is STATIC instead of collapse-aware ‚Üí the toolbar/stack stay pinned to the expanded footprint when both side panels are folded (observed: toolbar 792px stuck while ~600px sat unused each side); a side island goes full-height ‚Üí it covers the bottom-right gizmo/Persp-Ortho (they live within ~120px of the bottom edge); a panel mounted inside `<main>` forgets `stopPropagation` on contextmenu ‚Üí right-clicking it pops the Add menu; the narrow branch leaks into desktop (or omits an `isNarrow` guard) ‚Üí the desktop geometry shifts or the drawers/tabs render at wide widths. This is the inverse of the [[H91]]/[[V45]] family (a relocated surface silently overlaps another) generalized from spawned menus to the whole chrome layout. Type: STRUCTURAL (chrome-geometry). Sibling of [[V35]] (reveal reachable), [[V39]] (one glow reused), [[V45]] (one placement primitive).

**Enforcement:** `tests/e2e/ux2-floating-islands.spec.ts` ‚Äî viewport full-bleed (no reserved side columns / bottom rows); each side island is `position:absolute`, edge-hugging, top-anchored, bottom-clear; right-click on a panel does NOT open the Add menu (control: empty viewport does); the agent+timeline are a centered stack (chat above timeline); collapsing both side panels WIDENS the toolbar + stack (#2.8, follow-up 1); opening the timeline drawer hides the orbit hint (#2.9, follow-up 3); present mode hides every island. `tests/e2e/ux2-narrow-layout.spec.ts` (at 900px, follow-up 2) ‚Äî side panels off-canvas by default, edge tabs reveal them, the toolbar + stack go full-width, the edge tab slides a drawer in / scrim dismisses it, only one drawer open at a time, the Persp/Ortho pill is hidden, present hides the drawers/tabs/scrim; plus a wide control (no tabs/scrim, pill present at 1280px). Cross-ref [[V45]]/[[H91]] (the overlap family this generalizes), dharana [[B11]] (chrome re-validation). REF: `src/app/layoutIslands.ts` (geometry + breakpoint), `src/app/hooks/useIsNarrowLayout.ts` (the one breakpoint hook), `src/app/Layout.tsx` (island mounts + narrow drawers/tabs/scrim), `src/app/FloatingViewportToolbar.tsx` (collapse-aware + narrow full-width cap), `src/app/stores/chromeStore.ts` (ephemeral narrow drawer state), `src/app/LeftSidebar.tsx` + `src/app/NPanel.tsx` + `src/app/AgentDock.tsx` (transparent inner panels), `src/viewport/Viewport.tsx` (orbit-hint reposition + narrow-hide of gizmo/pill). Commits: side islands + bottom islands (UX #2 slices 1+2); follow-ups 1 (`ce950b7` collapse-aware reserve), 3 (`12f9a66` orbit-hint drawer guard), 2 (`8eecbf8` narrow breakpoint). Branch `ux-overhall`.

## V47 ‚Äî Scene environment (HDRI/IBL) is a DAG-resident Scene-level datum bound to `scene.environment`; it is NOT editor chrome, so it survives the render hide-pass and flows into the offscreen render automatically [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî UX-BACKLOG #9, 2026-06-15]

**The invariant (target):** the HDRI/environment config lives in the DAG as **Scene-node params** (decision 2026-06-15: Scene-level param, NOT a separate `EnvironmentLight` node) ‚Äî `envSource` (a discriminated source: `none` | `preset`:name | `file`:assetRef), `envIntensity`, `envRotationY`, `envBackground` ‚Äî so it is the ONE substrate (V34), saved/loaded/undone like any creative datum, never a viewport-only store. `Scene.evaluate` folds them into `SceneValue.environment`; the renderer mounts a drei `<Environment>` from the evaluated value, setting `scene.environment` (+ `scene.background` when the background toggle is on, `scene.environmentIntensity` / `scene.environmentRotation` from the params ‚Äî first-class three r169 props). Because `scene.environment` is a scene PROPERTY (not a traversed object), the `editorChrome` hide-pass (V37, `renderToImage.ts:139-151`) does NOT touch it ‚Üí the production render shows the same lighting with ZERO special-casing.

**Breaks when:** the env config is put in a viewport/chrome store instead of Scene params ‚Üí it is lost on save and undo, and `renderToImage` (which renders the live DAG scene) can't see a director's intent (V34 violation); the env is mounted/marked `editorChrome` ‚Üí it vanishes from the render (the inverse mistake ‚Äî chrome is hidden, env must NOT be); a NEW Scene param is read on the hydrate seam without a `?? default` ‚Üí an old project (envSource absent) crashes or renders black instead of `none` (the V10/H14 two-layer default rule ‚Äî default in the zod `.default('none')` AND at the renderer consumer); a **preset** source (drei fetches presets from a CDN at runtime) is treated as portable inside a `.basher` bundle ‚Äî it is NOT self-contained (only the `file`/OPFS-assetRef source embeds in the bundle, V41); two environments are wired (N/A for the Scene-param shape ‚Äî one-per-scene by construction, the reason the param shape was chosen over a list-of-lights node). Type: STRUCTURAL (substrate + render-parity). Sibling of [[V34]] (one substrate), [[V37]] (chrome excluded from render), [[V32]] (renderer is a compile target).

**Enforcement (SHIPPED 4 slices on `ux-overhall`, tips `4c0ffd0`‚Üí`7faab5f`):** node unit `src/nodes/Scene.test.ts` (folds preset/file ‚Üí `SceneValue.environment`; default `none`; back-compat no-env-fields). Store unit `src/app/asset/envHdriStore.test.ts` (content-hash path, dedupe, ext guard, load‚Üí`EquirectangularReflectionMapping`). Bundle unit `src/app/sceneBundle.test.ts` (collectAssetRefs picks up a `file` env, NOT a `preset`). E2E `tests/e2e/ux9-environment.spec.ts` (4): imported `.hdr` binds `scene.environment` + `scene.background` and CLEARS to none; the inspector control imports + binds (shows original filename); the env flows into the `renderToImage` output (V47 parity ‚Äî survives the chrome hide-pass); an imported HDRI embeds in the real `.basher` builder (V41). Files: `src/nodes/Scene.ts` (`envSource`/`envIntensity`/`envRotationY`/`envBackground` params, defaulted, version 1 ‚Äî no migration; `evaluate` folds with `?? default` = V10/H14 second layer), `src/nodes/types.ts` (`EnvironmentValue`/`EnvironmentSource`, `file` carries optional display `name`), `src/viewport/SceneEnvironment.tsx` (mounts drei `<Environment>` ‚Äî preset / file; NOT editorChrome) + `src/viewport/EnvironmentFile.tsx` + `src/app/asset/envHdriStore.ts` + `environmentTextureLoader.ts` (OPFS‚Üíequirect texture, mirrors bakedTexture), `src/app/SceneEnvironmentControls.tsx` (the inspector Environment section, primary domain), `src/app/sceneBundle.ts` (the `envHdri` ref category). GROUNDED NOTE: drei `setEnvProps` assigns `scene.environment = texture` DIRECTLY (no PMREM in the `map=` path) ‚Äî so the `file` texture MUST carry `EquirectangularReflectionMapping` (three processes the equirect env map at render); the blob URL has no extension, so the `map=` path (decode ourselves) is used, NOT `files=` (which picks the loader by extension). Decision source: AskUserQuestion 2026-06-15 (source = both presets + import; shape = Scene-level param). Status: **IMPLEMENTED.** Branch `ux-overhall`.
