**LIGHT consumer SHIPPED (#205, `8f7d22b`, 2026-06-19) ‚Äî the THIRD Track-To consumer.** Area lights aren't scene children, so `ConstrainedR` can't reach them ‚Äî they aim via `lookAt`, exactly like the camera. `useAreaLightAim` (SceneFromDAG) re-resolves the world aim PER FRAME via `resolveTrackToTarget` (the EditorViewCamera pattern ‚Äî snapshot DAG-state reads + live seconds + a stable local `EvaluatorCache`) and points the `RectAreaLight` (+ a studio light's emissive card) at it. Membership in `constraintTargetSet` is computed ONCE at the scene layer (O(N), B13) and passed as `constrained`, so an UNCONSTRAINED light spends a single boolean per frame and keeps its authored-`lookAt` `useEffect` (byte-identical to pre-#205); the per-frame path runs only for rigged lights. This IS the ¬ß7.2 LightRig ‚Äî the rig is a Track-To consumer, not a bespoke mechanism. Observed (`p205-studio-light.spec.ts`): a Track-To with a fixed aimPoint DISTINCT from the light's authored lookAt reorients the rendered RectAreaLight so its world forward (-Z) == `normalize(aimPoint ‚àí position)` ‚Äî the constraint provably overrides the authored lookAt; falsify = the forward is NOT the authored direction. SpotLight/DirectionalLight aiming is a trivial future extension (same `resolveTrackToTarget` feeds their `target`/rotation). Read-side note: a light's `lookAt` is not an inspector field today (AreaLight shows `transform` = position/rotation/scale), so there is no read-side desync to fold in ‚Äî unlike the camera/mesh. Status: **IMPLEMENTED (mesh + camera + light). The camera special case is deleted; the light rig is just a third consumer.**

## V61 ‚Äî A textured studio area light is a render-side PAIR (an illuminating RectAreaLight + an emissive textured card) reduced to ONE color via MEAN radiance; the DAG models it as the EXISTING AreaLight + an optional `tex`, NEVER a parallel `StudioLight` node [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #205]

**The invariant:** Blender-Light-Studio's signature object is a textured area emitter ‚Äî a real HDR card that both SHOWS its texture (the look + reflections) AND illuminates. three.js cannot do both in one object: a `RectAreaLight` illuminates but is an untexturable LTC approximation (one color, no shadows), and an emissive textured plane shows + reflects but doesn't light the raster scene. So a textured studio light is necessarily a **PAIR** in this renderer (`StudioAreaLightR`): a `RectAreaLight` tinted by the texture's MEAN radiance (`averageRadiance` ‚Üí `studioLightDrive`) PLUS an emissive textured card, both aimed at the same `lookAt` so the card is coplanar with the lit rectangle. The mean (the DC term) is the flux-faithful reduction ‚Äî Cycles never reduces (it importance-samples every texel); the reduction exists ONLY because the LTC light can't be textured, and the mean preserves the emitter's total flux. CRUCIALLY the pair is a RENDERER realization of ONE node: the DAG models the studio light as the EXISTING `AreaLight` + an OPTIONAL `tex` (an env-hdri assetRef, reusing the [[V47]]/V41 content-hash store ‚Äî never a second texture store), NOT a parallel `StudioLight` node ([[V34]]/[[V58]] ‚Äî one substrate, no second system). Unset `tex` ‚Üí byte-identical to a pre-#205 plain AreaLight (`PlainAreaLightR`; `tex` optional ‚Üí no migration). When the WebGPU/TSL path-tracer (v0.7 renderer epic) lands, the pair COLLAPSES to one real textured-area-light primitive with ZERO data-model change. Studio lights are ADDITIVE to the global HDRI ([[V47]]/¬ß1.4), never a replacement.

**Breaks when:** someone adds a parallel `StudioLight` node ‚Üí a second light system, the pair leaked into the data model, and the WebGPU upgrade needs a schema migration to merge it (the right move is `AreaLight` + `tex`, render-expanded); the texture‚Üílight reduction picks dominant-color or a GPU mip read instead of the CPU mean ‚Üí loses energy (dominant) or buys nothing but async plumbing (a 1√ó1 mip IS the mean); the reduction reads RAW half-float bits instead of decoding them ([[H109]]) ‚Üí the chroma is wrong (half-float storage is non-linear in its bits); a second texture store is invented for the light `tex` instead of reusing the env-hdri store ‚Üí divergent persistence/`.basher` embed; the emissive card is flagged editorChrome ‚Üí it vanishes from the offscreen render (it's the light's real look, must appear, [[V37]]); the card steals viewport clicks ‚Üí selection breaks (raycast disabled); shadows are faked with a proxy now ‚Üí work the path-tracer makes obsolete (v1 accepts no area-light shadows ‚Äî known-limit). Type: STRUCTURAL+DATA-FLOW (one node, render-expanded pair; pure reduction shared viewport‚Üîoffscreen). Sibling of [[V58]]/[[V60]] (the operator/constraint substrate + the rig aim), [[V47]] (the env HDRI store + the global IBL layer studio lights add to), [[V37]] (render parity ‚Äî the same reduction feeds viewport + offscreen), [[V34]] (one substrate, no parallel node).

**Enforcement (#205 SHIPPED, 2026-06-19, `ux-overhall` `a7b47e2`):** `src/app/averageRadiance.ts` (`averageRadiance` + `studioLightDrive`, 8 unit ‚Äî uniform/mixed/HDR-magnitude/half-float-decode/empty-neutral + the unit-luminance chroma split); `AreaLight` node `tex?` param + `AreaLightValue.tex?` (optional ‚Üí no migration); `StudioAreaLightR` (SceneFromDAG) render-expands the pair, branch on a COMPONENT boundary (`PlainAreaLightR`/`StudioAreaLightR`) so each path's hooks stay unconditional and only the textured path suspends on the env-texture decode. Observed (`p205-studio-light.spec.ts`, REAL render): a textured AreaLight grows BOTH a RectAreaLight AND an emissive card whose texture's mean-radiance CHROMA == the live RectAreaLight's color chroma (render-side == resolver-side, the card's own half-float texels decoded + averaged independently in-test); a plain AreaLight renders NO card (falsification); the offscreen render succeeds with the studio light present ([[V37]]). KNOWN-LIMITS (v1, renderer-approximate per ¬ß1.5): no area-light shadows (deferred to the path-tracer); the equirect `tex` is sampled by UV on the flat card (shows the lat-long image); no inspector control to SET `tex` yet (set via the agent/e2e seam today ‚Äî the authoring UI is the #206 2D panel). The emission params (opacity/falloff/saturation/mute) are deferred to their first consumer (#206 panel ‚Äî Vairagya). Status: **IMPLEMENTED.**

## V62 ‚Äî The 2D Light-Studio panel is a single-pure-resolver authoring surface: it places rig lights through `resolveStudioLightTransform` (forward) and draws them through its inverse `studioLightPanelXY`, so puck == light == render [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #206]

**The invariant:** The Light-Studio panel (¬ß7.3) is a lat-long (equirectangular) flattening of the rig sphere around a derived centre. Its WHOLE coordinate translation is ONE pure mapping and its inverse: `resolveStudioLightTransform(panelXY, radius, target) ‚Üí {position}` places a light on the sphere; `studioLightPanelXY(position, target) ‚Üí {panelXY, radius}` projects an existing light back to its puck. The panel renders pucks through the inverse and authors drags through the forward ‚Äî so the puck a director sees, the world position the renderer lights from, and the spot a "+ Light"/drag lands at are all the SAME function ([[V51]]/[[V56]] one-pure-resolver shape). The panel never bakes a parallel azimuth/elevation table. Orientation is NOT the panel's job ‚Äî a rig light is an `AreaLight` aimed by a Track-To ([[V60]]); the panel owns placement only, and the light keeps facing the centre via its constraint. A rig light = an AreaLight that a Track-To targets ([[V60]]/`enumerateStudioLights`); a free fill light is NOT on the rig and draws no puck. The rig CENTRE is DERIVED from the lights' shared Track-To aim (`resolveRigTarget`, default world origin), not stored ‚Äî an explicit `LightRig` node is deferred to #208 profiles. The screen‚ÜîpanelXY pixel mapping (the v-flip) lives in ONE module (`studioPanelGeometry`) shared by the component AND its e2e ([[H95]] ‚Äî one geometry source). The tex picker reuses `importEnvironmentHdri` (the [[V47]] env-HDRI store), NEVER a second texture store.

**Breaks when:** the panel computes puck positions with its own trig instead of `studioLightPanelXY` ‚Üí puck ‚âÝ where the light renders (the V37 parity break the one-resolver shape exists to prevent); a drag writes position by an ad-hoc inverse instead of `resolveStudioLightTransform` ‚Üí drag-to-place desyncs from the puck; the screen‚ÜîpanelXY mapping is duplicated in the e2e ‚Üí it silently drifts from the component and targets the wrong pixel ([[H95]]); the panel introduces a parallel `StudioLight`/`LightRig` node instead of deriving the rig from existing Track-To aims ([[V61]]/[[V34]] ‚Äî one substrate); the panel bakes a rotation instead of leaving orientation to the light's Track-To ([[V60]]); the EvaluatorCache feeding `resolveRigTarget` is memoized once and reused across DAG edits ‚Üí a moved aim-node yields a STALE rig centre (build a fresh cache per reactive recompute); a per-light param control invents a second mutation path instead of a `setParam` Op ‚Üí it doesn't save/undo/animate ([[V1]]/[[V57]]). Type: STRUCTURAL+DATA-FLOW (one resolver both directions; render==puck==author; one geometry source). Sibling of [[V60]] (the aim the placement pairs with), [[V61]] (the studio light it authors), [[V51]]/[[V56]] (the one-pure-resolver shape), [[V37]] (panel==viewport), [[V47]] (the env store the tex picker reuses).

**#208 addendum (2026-06-19):** the explicit `LightRig` node (deferred above) has now LANDED ‚Äî see [[V63]]. The rig now OWNS an explicit `center`/`radius`; `resolveRigTarget`'s derived centre remains the panel's fallback until the panel is wired to read the active rig's explicit centre (a #208 UI increment).

**Enforcement (#206 SHIPPED, 2026-06-19, `ux-overhall` `aedf704`‚Üí`8024f4b`):** increment 1 `src/app/resolveStudioLightTransform.ts` (forward + inverse, 9 unit, round-trip exact). UI: `src/timeline/LightStudioPanel.tsx` (a third timeline-drawer tab ‚Äî Dopesheet|Curve|Light Studio, the keyframe toolbar hidden on this spatial tab) reads via `src/app/studioLightRig.ts` (`enumerateStudioLights` = Track-To-aimed AreaLights only; `resolveRigTarget` = shared aim, default origin, FRESH cache per recompute) and `src/timeline/studioPanelGeometry.ts` (the v-flip, [[H95]] one source). Drag = pointer-capture ‚Üí `fractionToPanelXY` ‚Üí `resolveStudioLightTransform` ‚Üí `setParam` position (radius frozen at grab). "+ Light" = `src/app/addStudioLight.ts` (`buildAddStudioLightOps` ‚Äî atomic AreaLight‚Üíscene.lights + Track-To aiming the centre, spawned through the same placement core). Per-light params + the emitter-tex picker (`StudioLightControls`, reusing `importEnvironmentHdri`) ‚Äî CLOSES the #205 no-tex-picker known-limit. Observed (`p206-light-studio-panel.spec.ts`, LIVE app): a puck lands at `panelXYToFraction(studioLightPanelXY(pos, target))` (panel==resolver); dragging a puck to a known canvas fraction sets the light's DAG position == the resolver output AND moves a live RectAreaLight there (panel==viewport, V37); "+ Light" yields a puck+row+selected controls; the tex picker makes a live emissive card appear (the ¬ß1.5 pair) ‚Äî falsified by a free light (no puck) + a plain light (no card). KNOWN-LIMIT (v1): no ‚óá keyframe-diamond IN the panel (a custom control bypasses the generic diamond, [[H104]]) ‚Äî params are animatable from the dopesheet/inspector, just not keyable from this surface yet; the env-HDRI backdrop on the canvas + profiles/`LightRig` node (#208) are later slices. Status: **IMPLEMENTED.**

## V63 ‚Äî A lighting PROFILE is a `LightRig` node (groups its lights + owns the shared aim centre/radius); profiles are SWITCHED by a `LightProfileSelect` (one named rig live at a time), ALL co-resident in the DAG ‚Äî never a parallel store [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #208 COMPLETE: substrate + Profiles-bar UI + JSON I/O]

**The invariant:** A named, switchable lighting setup (¬ß7.5, the `.bls` profile concept) lives ENTIRELY on the one substrate ([[V34]]/[[V58]] ‚Äî a `NodeDefinition` + typed sockets, no second store). One `LightRig` = one profile: it GROUPS its lights (a `Light` list input) and OWNS the shared aim `center` + `radius` the panel's pucks orbit (formalizing the centre [[V62]]/`resolveRigTarget` previously DERIVED from the lights' shared Track-To aim). A `LightProfileSelect` (the [[ClipSelect]] pattern) takes N rigs and exposes the one whose `name` == its `selectedProfile` param on a single output ‚Üí `Scene.inputs.lightRig`; so exactly one profile is live while every profile stays resident in the DAG. Switching is ONE `setParam` ‚Üí keyframeable for free ([[V57]]: a shot can ANIMATE between lighting setups, beyond BLS). `Scene` keeps the rig SEPARATE from its direct `lights` (a distinct `lightRig` input + `SceneValue.lightRig`) so the direct-light index-correspondence stays byte-identical; the renderer renders `lightRig.lights` as a PARALLEL band and recovers each rig light's node id by edge-order via `resolveRigLightSources` (the SAME index-correspondence the direct lights hold), so Track-To aim ([[V60]]) + click-select keep working for rig lights. null-on-miss in the select is deliberate (a gone profile is visible, not silently the first rig).

**Breaks when:** a profile is stored as an app-layer JSON snapshot OUTSIDE the DAG instead of a co-resident subgraph ‚Üí a second source of truth ([[V34]] break ‚Äî the option the user explicitly rejected); the rig's lights are MERGED into `Scene.lights` instead of a separate band ‚Üí the direct-light index-correspondence with `Scene.inputs.lights` misaligns and aim/click-select target the wrong node; `resolveRigLightSources` derives ids by a re-walk/name instead of the rig's `inputs.lights` edge order ‚Üí drifts from `LightRig.evaluate`'s light order ([[V44]] sibling ‚Äî key by stable index, not re-derivation); the select falls back to the first rig on miss ‚Üí a deleted profile silently renders the wrong lights; switching links/unlinks edges instead of one param ‚Üí not keyframeable (the link/unlink option, also rejected). Type: STRUCTURAL+DATA-FLOW (one substrate; co-resident; index-correspondence preserved across a new band). Sibling of [[V62]] (the panel that authors a rig's lights), [[V60]] (the aim each rig light keeps), [[ClipSelect]]/[[V57]] (the switch-by-param shape), [[V34]]/[[V58]] (one substrate).

**Enforcement (#208 increments 1‚Äì2 SHIPPED, 2026-06-19, `ux-overhall` `a084422`/`ae2739f`):** `src/nodes/LightRig.ts` (the rig node ‚Äî `LightRigValue` + the `'LightRig'` socket type; groups lights + center/radius); `src/nodes/LightProfileSelect.ts` (the switch ‚Äî ClipSelect-pattern, picks by `selectedProfile`, null-on-miss); `src/nodes/Scene.ts` (a SEPARATE `lightRig` input ‚Üí `SceneValue.lightRig`, never merged); `src/app/resolveRigLightSources.ts` (`resolveActiveRigNode` follows Scene‚Üíselect‚Üínamed-rig; `resolveRigLightSources` returns the rig's light node ids in edge order); `src/viewport/SceneFromDAG.tsx` (the parallel rig-light render band + helpers). Observed (`p208-light-rig.spec.ts`, LIVE app): a rig wired to `scene.lightRig` renders both grouped lights AND a Track-To still aims one (proves node-id recovery ‚Äî the aim only fires if `constraintTargets.has(recoveredId)`); a `LightProfileSelect` flips the live profile by one `setParam` ("Key" 2-light ‚Üí "Rim" 1-light); an unwired rig renders nothing (falsification); offscreen render parity holds (V37). 9 unit (LightRig 3 + LightProfileSelect 4 + resolveRigLightSources 2). KNOWN-LIMITS (substrate done, app-layer pending): no "+ Profile" builder / profile-switcher UI yet; existing studio lights aren't yet migrated into a default rig; the panel still enumerates lights from ALL rigs (not just the active profile) and `resolveRigTarget` still derives the centre rather than reading the rig's explicit `center`; JSON import/export (#208 final increment) not yet built. Status: **IMPLEMENTED (substrate); app-layer authoring + JSON I/O pending.**

**#208 app-layer + JSON I/O addendum (increments 3‚Äì4, `c4a047c`/`ca08154`/`463907a`, 2026-06-19) ‚Äî grounded in BLS `light_profiles.py` + `gui.py` (read end-to-end at `/tmp/bls-study`):** the BLS "Profiles" panel maps onto Basher's substrate as a **Profiles bar atop the Light Studio tab** (HDR Light Studio + BLS both keep setup management WITH the canvas, never a generic inspector ‚Äî the user picked this via AskUserQuestion). `src/app/studioProfiles.ts` = the reader (`enumerateProfiles`, `activeProfileSelect`) + atomic Op-builders: `buildAddProfileOps` (create rig + wire a `LightProfileSelect`‚Üíscene on the first profile, activate it, and ADOPT legacy free studio lights ‚Äî disconnect from `scene.lights`, connect to `rig.lights` ‚Äî so existing setups don't vanish once the panel scopes), `buildSelectProfileOp` (one keyframeable setParam), `buildDeleteProfileOps` (remove the rig + its light subtree + their Track-Tos, re-point the select to a survivor ‚Äî respecting `removeNode`'s "refuse while consumed" rule by disconnecting first), `uniqueProfileName` (the SHARED collision guard both the add path and JSON import route through ‚Äî the select keys by NAME, so a duplicate is ambiguous). The panel is now profile-aware: `enumerateActiveProfileLights` (active rig's lights in edge order, else legacy fallback) + `resolveActiveRigCenter` (the rig's explicit `center`, else derived). `src/app/studioProfileIO.ts` = the portable `.bls`-shaped JSON (`{format, version, profiles:[{name, center, radius, lights:[‚Ä¶]}]}`): `composeProfile`/`composeProfilesFile` (serialize), `parseProfilesFile` (zod-validate), `buildImportProfilesOps` (rebuild rigs+lights+Track-Tos, de-dupe names). Observed (LIVE): `p208-profiles-ui` (add‚Üí2 lights‚Üíempty 2nd profile‚Üíswitch re-scopes 2‚Üî1‚Üídelete re-points), `p208-profiles-io` (Import rebuilds a 2-light profile + names the switcher; malformed file ‚Üí error, no nodes). Texture portability: a light's `tex` ref is carried (portable within the same OPFS ‚Äî copy-between-scenes); cross-app needs the bytes (the `.basher` bundle's job, V41). REMAINING KNOWN-LIMITS: no rename-in-place (rename needs rig.name + select.selectedProfile updated together ‚Äî deferred); Export writes ALL profiles only (no "export selected"); the env-HDRI canvas backdrop is still a later nicety; no ‚óá keying IN the panel ([[H104]]). Status: **IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #208 COMPLETE (substrate + app-layer authoring + JSON I/O).**

**The Light Brush (#207, `da8af37`‚Üí`f7d77f4`) is a SECOND surface onto the same coordinate system ‚Äî the invariant generalizes.** A viewport modal (`lightBrushStore`, transient like the gizmo flag): while active, a mesh click PAINTS the selected rig light onto the rig sphere via `resolveLightBrushPlacement` (the ¬ß7.4 pure core ‚Äî reflect(viewDir, normal) for a highlight, or the normal, intersected with the SAME rig sphere the panel drags on, radius preserved). So drag (panel) and brush (viewport) write the light through resolvers that share ONE sphere/shell ‚Äî `studioLightPanelXY` projects EITHER back to the same puck ‚Äî and the light keeps aiming at centre via its Track-To ([[V60]]). The decision layer `buildLightBrushOp` is pure over (state, seconds, selection, hit) ‚Üí testable; the impure shell (extract hit / world-normal / view-ray from the R3F event) is a thin branch in `SceneFromDAG`'s `onClick`; `onPointerMissed` is guarded so a missed stroke keeps the selected light. Observed (`p207-light-brush.spec.ts`, LIVE app): brush-on click moves the light onto its radius-shell AND a live RectAreaLight follows (panel==viewport); brush-off click leaves it (falsification). New trap [[H110]] (an e2e viewport click can land on a floating DOM island / editor helper over the canvas ‚Äî verify the hit target). **Breaks additionally when:** the brush re-implements the rig sphere instead of reusing the placement core (drift from the panel's coordinate system); the brush bakes orientation instead of leaving it to the Track-To; a missed stroke deselects the light mid-painting (guard `onPointerMissed`). KNOWN-LIMIT: the brush only paints onto `SceneChildNode` meshes (clicking a helper selects it); non-uniform-scaled normals use `transformDirection` (not inverse-transpose) ‚Äî fine for typical subjects.

## V64 ‚Äî A geometry MODIFIER (SOP) is a Mesh‚ÜíMesh wrapper sub-chain node producing a REBUILDABLE `GeometryRef` handle; ONE shared projection builds the descriptor key on BOTH the evaluate road and the read-side road, so render==resolver; the `OperatorStack` is the chain-wiring sugar [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #209]

**The invariant:** A geometry modifier (the SOP half of [[V58]]) IS the doc ¬ß2.2 wrapper sub-chain node ([[V60]] proved a _constraint_ is NOT ‚Äî it needs world position ‚Äî but a modifier needs only the mesh VALUE, so it fits): a `NodeDefinition` with a `Mesh target` input + `Mesh out` output (`ArrayModifier`, `src/nodes/ArrayModifier.ts`), edge-WIRED `base ‚Üí mod ‚Üí consumer`. Its `evaluate` projects the source mesh value to a source `GeometryRef`, wraps it in a RECURSIVE descriptor (`{kind:'array', source, count, offset}`), and emits a `ModifiedMeshValue` carrying that handle + the INHERITED source TRS/material (the modifier rewrites geometry in local space; the source's transform positions the whole result). The handle is REBUILDABLE from params ‚Äî `geometryRegistry.build` recurses into the source then applies the op (SYNC; clone-don't-mutate the cached source) ‚Äî UNLIKE a baked OPFS handle (no suspense). The renderer (`ModifiedMeshR`) reads it via `geometryRegistry.get` and the read-side (`resolveEvaluatedMesh` recursive branch) wraps the SAME way through the ONE shared `src/app/modifierGeometry.ts` (`sourceGeometryRef`/`arrayGeometryRef`) ‚Üí the descriptor key is byte-identical on both roads (render==resolver, [[H40]] one band, [[V37]] parity). `muted` is identity passthrough at evaluate (the stack bypass). The ONE new shared abstraction ¬ß2.2 names is `OperatorStack` (`src/app/operatorStack.ts`) ‚Äî enumerate/add/remove/reorder/mute as pure Op chains over the sub-chain (reorder = re-wire); the UI (`ModifierStackControls`) and the agent (`mutator.geometry.addModifier`) both author through it, one wiring authority. The doc's "polymorphic over transform+geometry" COLLAPSED: constraints are edge-less (scene layer), so `OperatorStack` serves the geometry stack ONLY.

**Breaks when:** a modifier inlines geometry buffers instead of a `GeometryRef` handle ‚Üí heavy buffers leak into Ops/undo/hashing ([[V43]] cost class); the evaluate road and the read-side road build the descriptor key DIFFERENTLY (two ad-hoc projections instead of `modifierGeometry.ts`) ‚Üí render‚âÝresolver, the gizmo/inspector see a different mesh than the viewport ([[H40]]); the registry `build('array')` MUTATES the cached source geometry instead of cloning each copy ‚Üí every other ref sharing that source is corrupted (the cache is shared by deterministic key); a modifier emits the geometry inline as a primitive (it CAN'T ‚Äî modified geometry isn't a box/sphere param) instead of a handle-carrying value; `muted` is handled in the renderer instead of as an evaluate passthrough ‚Üí the read-side and offscreen render disagree on the bypass; a glTF/baked source (async, outside the sync registry) is force-built ‚Üí `get` returns null and the array renders nothing (v1 passes the source THROUGH ‚Äî a clean follow-up); the OperatorStack's reorder/remove forgets to splice the chain closed (disconnect both edges + reconnect neighbours, respect `removeNode` refuse-while-consumed). Type: STRUCTURAL+DATA-FLOW (handle not buffers; one projection two roads; sub-chain wiring). Sibling of [[V58]] (the substrate ‚Äî this is its SOP half), [[V60]] (the CHOP half ‚Äî the edge-less contrast that PROVED the sub-chain fits geometry), [[V37]]/[[H40]] (render==resolver, one band), [[V34]] (one substrate ‚Äî a modifier is a `NodeDefinition`, not a new engine), [[V57]] (count/offset/muted are free-floating-channel animatable).

**Enforcement:** IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #209 (`2f0537e` operator + `f7e2bbf` OperatorStack + `9304876` stack UI + `fdd4886` agent op). Observed (LIVE, `p209-array-modifier` + `p209-modifier-stack-ui`): Box‚ÜíArray‚ÜíScene renders the merged array, render verts == resolver verts (`__basher_modified_vertex_count`); a 2-deep chain renders cumulatively (recursive build); the panel's "+ Array"/mute/delete drive the live render. Unit: registry array build (count√ó verts, translated bounds, no source mutation), evaluate‚Üîresolve key parity, OperatorStack add-between/stack-on-top/splice/reorder/mute, the agent op through all five gates.

**GENERALIZATION PROVEN ‚Äî `MirrorModifier`, the SECOND geometry operator (`582a327`, post-#209).** The substrate's claim ("a new modifier = a node + a `build` branch + the shared projection key + a read-side parity twin + four one-line registrations: `MODIFIER_NODE_TYPES`, `registerAll`, the `ADDABLE` UI list, the agent `ModifierType` enum") was VERIFIED by adding Mirror with ZERO changes to the OperatorStack, `ModifiedMeshR`, or `resolveEvaluatedMesh`'s recursion machinery. Mirror reflects the source across the plane ‚üÇ`axis` at `offset` and merges ‚Üí 2√ó verts. It exercises a build mechanism Array did NOT: a determinant‚àí1 transform, which **flips triangle winding** ‚Üí the reflected half MUST have its winding reversed (`reverseWinding` in `geometryRegistry.build('mirror')`) or it renders inside-out (the normals are reflected by `applyMatrix4` but the index order would disagree). The new sub-pattern: **a reflecting/orientation-flipping geometry op reverses the winding of any det‚àí1 copy** ([[H112]]). Observed (LIVE, `p209-mirror-modifier` + a face-orientation unit test + a render PNG showing two solid, correctly-lit boxes): render verts 48 == resolver; mute falsifies to 24; a MIXED Array‚ÜíMirror chain composes to 144; every reflected face's winding agrees with its normal. `offset` (default 0 = Blender origin-mirror) separates the halves so the modifier isn't a visual no-op on v1's geometry-centered primitives.

**KNOWN-LIMITS (clean future slices):** Array + Mirror in v1 (Subdivide/Solidify register a type + a `build` branch); the agent op is add-only (remove/reorder/mute via the UI or `dag.exec` setParam). **[RESOLVED `3cdc0bb`] `ModifiedMesh` UVs are no longer null ‚Äî the Array/Mirror read-side branches run the SAME `resolveRegistryUVs` Box/Sphere use (the modified geometry is sync-buildable), so the UV-editor backdrop works for a modifier.** **[RESOLVED `12b5f64`] the gizmo on a selected modifier is no longer inert ‚Äî `Gizmo.tsx` derives its transform TARGET via `resolveStackBase` (a modifier selection ‚Üí the base mesh), so it mounts at the base + a grab moves the base + the whole modified result; selection stays on the modifier. Observed LIVE (`p209-gizmo-on-modifier`). Caveat: an ANIMATED base under a modifier seeds from the static authored transform (resolver is null when the base isn't a direct scene child).** **[DEFERRED ‚Äî a real feature slice, NOT cleanup] glTF/baked modifier sources still pass through: a modifier's geometry build is SYNC (`geometryRegistry.get`), but a baked source's bytes are async-OPFS and a glTF child's geometry lives in the asset CLONE the registry deliberately doesn't own ([[H45]]). Baked = moderate (recursive Suspense in `ModifiedMeshR` reusing `bakedGeometryLoader` ‚Üí prime ‚Üí build); glTF = larger (cross the asset-clone boundary). Its own slice; surfaced to the user.** **[RESOLVED `4a39ea6`] a string-ENUM param (Mirror's `axis`) used to render READ-ONLY in the generic inspector ‚Äî now `NPanel`'s `ParamRow` reads the node's zod `paramSchema`: a top-level string param that unwraps to a `ZodEnum` renders an `EnumField` `<select>` (a free string still renders read-only). Unlocked Mirror's `axis` + every other top-level enum param (`RenderOutput.tonemap`, `TransformClip.loop`, `VideoStitch.codec`, ‚Ä¶). Observed LIVE (`inspector-enum-param` e2e, UI‚ÜísetParam‚ÜíDAG‚Üírender): the axis dropdown flips the rendered mesh span x‚âà5‚Üíy‚âà5. Enum params still get no keyframe ‚óá (discrete config, like the `muted` boolean ‚Äî keyable from the dopesheet if ever needed; the residual H104-adjacent slice).**

## V65 ‚Äî One shared viewport selection handler (`selectNodeOnClick`) drives EVERY picker; a renderable inherits click-to-select by calling it, never by copy-pasting the rule [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #211 part 4.1]

**The invariant:** click-to-select a viewport object is ONE rule ‚Äî stopPropagation + `select`/`selectAdditive(pickId)`, a null `pickId` a no-op that does NOT stopPropagation (so an unroutable click falls through to OrbitControls) ‚Äî owned by `src/viewport/selectNodeOnClick.ts` (`selectNode` core + `selectNodeOnClick` handler factory). Every picker calls it: `LightHelpers` (4 helpers), `CameraHelper`, and `SceneChildNode` (which layers its Light-Brush gate + drill-context reset AROUND the shared `selectNode`). A new renderable kind becomes selectable by calling one helper, not by re-deriving the rule. Part of the renderable-node-protocol unification ([[V59]] world-transform, the animation-overlay seam) ‚Äî the consumer-layer concerns that were per-type collapse onto shared seams.

**Breaks when:** a new picker copy-pastes the select block ‚Üí the rule drifts (e.g. forgets stopPropagation ‚Üí OrbitControls double-acts, or forgets shift-additive ‚Üí multi-select breaks for that kind); a picker stopPropagations on a null pickId ‚Üí an unroutable click is swallowed instead of falling through. Type: STRUCTURAL (one seam, N callers ‚Äî the [[H40]]-style "one band, many consumers" shape applied to selection). Sibling of [[V59]] (uniform world transform), [[V57]] (one overlay primitive). NOTE: the render-dispatch _collapse_ (the 3 `.map` bands ‚Üí one tagged list) was DELIBERATELY NOT done (#211 part 4.2) ‚Äî high risk (V37 index-correspondence + H48 memo) for a dev-velocity-only benefit, and lights vs meshes are genuinely different render primitives; "render-dispatch unification" is realized as the cross-cutting concerns (picking here; animation via the future seam) being shared, bands stay. Enforcement: `selectNodeOnClick.test.ts` (4 unit ‚Äî select / shift-additive / null no-op-no-stopProp / handler); observed LIVE via p165 (camera frustum select), p207 (brush gate + falsification), ux7 (mesh drill-select). Status: **IMPLEMENTED (4.1); 4.2 render-dispatch collapse intentionally out of scope.**

## V66 ‚Äî Browser file access is CAPABILITY-based, not PATH-based: a single-file pick yields bytes+basename only (no path, no siblings), so multi-file glTF needs a DIRECTORY grant; and a folder with >1 glTF entry MUST let the user disambiguate, never silently auto-pick [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #215]

**The invariant:** in a browser, importing a file grants a CAPABILITY over exactly the thing the user designated, not a path you can navigate from. A `<input type=file>` / `showOpenFilePicker()` selection gives a `File`/handle with bytes + basename and NO directory/path (`File.path` doesn't exist on the web; `webkitRelativePath` is `''` for a single-file pick; a file handle has no parent). So a multi-file `.gltf` (external `.bin`/textures referenced by relative URI) can ONLY be read by granting the DIRECTORY ‚Äî `showDirectoryPicker`, `webkitdirectory`, or a folder DROP (`webkitGetAsEntry` on a dropped _folder_). This is invariant across all three APIs; a file grant can never be promoted to sibling/folder access. The only single-file-self-sufficient form is `.glb` (embedded). Corollary (the addressable part Basher CAN own): when a granted folder contains MORE THAN ONE glTF entry, the importer must let the user choose which to import ‚Äî never silently auto-pick ‚Äî because `locateEntryFile`'s "shallowest, then first" is browser-enumeration-order nondeterministic and routinely picks a stripped/untextured variant over the real model.

**Breaks when:** code tries to "pick the file then read its folder" (there is no folder to read ‚Äî the path was never given; native DCCs like Blender can because they're native + path-based, the web is not); a multi-entry folder is auto-resolved to one entry with no UI (the silent-wrong-entry trap, [[H113]]); the entry chooser is wired into ONE import path but not the others (menu picker, drag-drop, e2e seam diverge) instead of a single shared chokepoint; the agent/headless path is made to block on the modal (it must keep auto-locate). Type: STRUCTURAL (a browser-platform boundary fact) + the one-chokepoint discipline ([[H40]]-style). Enforcement (#215, 2026-06-21, `ux-overhall` `f03c0de`): `gltfEntryChooserStore` + `GltfEntryChooser` (promise-based modal, mounted in App, mirrors renderAnimationStore/RenderAnimationProgress); `summarizeGltfEntry` shows per-entry material/texture counts (richest-first, top-focused) so the textured model is obvious; ONE shared `gltfEntryChoice.ingestAndImportGltf` (resolve choice ‚Üí ingest once ‚Üí import) consumed by menu picker + drag-drop + the `__basher_ingestGltfFolder` e2e seam; `ingestGltfFolder` gains an optional `preferredEntryRelativePath` to honor the choice (default ‚Üí auto-locate); agent + pure callers keep auto-locate (no modal). 1 entry ‚Üí no prompt (byte-identical to before). 8 unit + 2 e2e (`gltf-multi-entry-chooser.spec.ts`); 23 import/drop e2e green. Sibling of [[V23]] (the multi-file sibling-path resolver this boundary feeds), [[V53]] (the spec/gloss conversion at the same ingest seam). **IMPORT-ALL SHIPPED (#219, 2026-06-22, `ux-overhall` `e1a72f1`):** the single-select chooser gained an "Import all N as separate models" action ‚Äî the store's choice became a tagged union (`{type:'one'|'all'}|null`) + a `chooseAll()` resolver; `resolveGltfEntryChoice` maps "all" ‚Üí `{ all: [...richest-first relativePaths] }`; the chokepoint `ingestAndImportGltf` loops, ingesting EACH entry into its OWN resolved folder (named by the entry's filename stem) so per-entry spec/gloss conversion + baked sibling textures stay ISOLATED (no cross-entry `basher-mr-<mat>.png` collision ‚Äî the reason NOT to share one folder). 1 entry ‚Üí no prompt; single-pick shape unchanged (callers + tests untouched). KNOWN-LIMIT (v1): entries sharing heavy assets duplicate those bytes per model (the trade-off for isolation simplicity; a write-once-shared-folder pass is a follow-up). +1 unit (chooseAll ‚Üí `{all: richest-first}`) + e2e ("import all" ‚Üí 2 GltfAsset models in the DAG). vitest 1856. Status: **IMPLEMENTED.**

## V67 ‚Äî A Group is transformable as a unit (Blender's parent/Empty); the glTF-import root is ONE transformable Group with a bbox-centre pivot ‚Äî never a non-transformable wrapper over a separate Transform [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #222]

**The invariant:** a `Group` carries its OWN `position/rotation/scale` plus a local `pivot`, and the renderer applies `Translate(position)¬∑R¬∑S¬∑Translate(-pivot)` (`GroupR`, an inner `<group position={-pivot}>`). The glTF import (`buildGltfImportOps`) and the catalog drop (`buildAssetDropOps`) both wire `GltfAsset ‚Üí Group ‚Üí Scene` ‚Äî the Group IS the single transformable import root (Blender's parent/Empty model: `io_scene_gltf2/blender/imp/node.py:50-101` ‚Äî one object per glTF node, each carrying its own TRS; the synthetic DummyRoot is NOT materialised, `node.py:42-44`; the scene is organised by a non-transformable Collection). There is NO separate `Transform` wrapper in the import chain. The import bakes `pivot =` the model's world bbox centre (`computeGltfBoundsCenter`, pure, from glTF accessor min/max ‚Äî NO buffer reads) and `position = drop + pivot`, so the content stays where authored while the gizmo sits at the model centre and rotation/scale happen about that centre. Because `getManipulable` reads `params.position` and `resolveEvaluatedTransform` reads `value.position`, both light up automatically and the pivot is transparent to them ‚Üí render == gizmo == inspector ([[V37]]/[[H40]]) with no extra wiring. `resolveWorldTransform.localMatrix` composes the SAME pivot-aware matrix so world-transform/Track-To parity ([[V59]]) holds.

**Breaks when:** the import re-introduces a separate Transform wrapper (the parent the user selects becomes non-manipulable again ‚Äî [[H115]]); a SECOND node also owns the transform (e.g. adding TRS to GltfAsset while keeping the Group transform ‚Üí V20 one-writer violation); `GroupR` rotates/scales WITHOUT the pivot inner-offset (the model rotates about the world origin, not its centre); the bbox centre is computed from the live three clone instead of the glTF accessors (render-time ‚Üí DAG write, a [[V34]] boundary violation, and async so the gizmo can't seed); the new params are added without a [[V10]]/[[H14]] layer-2 default at the evaluator AND consumer (an OLD saved Group is NOT re-parsed by `migrateOneNode` ‚Äî version unchanged ‚Äî so the zod `.default` never fires and the renderer destructures `undefined pivot` ‚Üí load crash). Type: STRUCTURAL (one transformable import root; Blender parity). Sibling of [[V37]] (viewport==render), [[V59]] (world transform), [[H40]] (render==gizmo==inspector), [[H115]] (the no-gizmo-on-wrapper diagnosis), [[V53]]/[[V66]] (the same ingest seam).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#222, 2026-06-22, `ux-overhall` `476274a`‚Üí`afc27ec`, 3 slices). Slice 1 `476274a` (Group gains transform + pivot, GroupR + resolveWorldTransform pivot-aware, inspectorSections gains 'transform'); slice 2/3 `a600978` (import root = one transformable Group, `computeGltfBoundsCenter` pivot, dropChain aligned, legacy `tx` kept in importGroupNodeIds for old-save delete-cascade); self-review `afc27ec` (V10/H14 layer-2 default for legacy Groups). Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest 1877; e2e `gltf-import-group-gizmo` (select import group ‚Üí gizmo mounts + resolver position) + 22 import/anim/child/outliner regression green. OBSERVED (real horse): import ‚Üí ONE Group root (0 Transforms), pivot = bbox centre [~0, 60.2, 2.07].

## V68 ‚Äî A manipulator (gizmo) operates in the space the object RENDERS in: it seeds at the node's WORLD transform and converts a drag back to the authored (LOCAL) param space on write ‚Äî render == gizmo == inspector holds for the manipulation ROUND-TRIP, not just the read

**The invariant:** the transform gizmo's proxy is anchored at the node's WORLD pose (`parentWorld ¬∑ localMatrix(node)`), so it sits exactly where the object renders, and every drag is converted back to the node's LOCAL params (`parentWorld‚Åª¬π ¬∑ proxyWorld`, stripping a dragged Group's own `-pivot`) before dispatch. The parent world comes from ONE pure resolver ‚Äî `resolveParentWorldMatrix` (`src/app/resolveWorldTransform.ts`) ‚Äî which mirrors the SceneFromDAG composition (incl. Group pivot + the SAME channel/transient overlay the renderer applies, one band [[H40]]). It returns null for a top-level child (parent = identity scene root), a flat light/camera (never nested), and an unresolvable node (a GltfChild's world is name-addressed inside the GltfAsset, not a scene-child edge) ‚Üí the gizmo keeps the LOCAL path, byte-identical. This extends [[V37]] (viewport==render) and [[H40]] (read==render) from the READ surfaces (gizmo display, inspector display) to the WRITE round-trip: the manipulator both _shows_ and _edits_ in render space while the substrate stores authored-local params ([[V34]]).

**Breaks when:** the gizmo seeds from the LOCAL transform (`resolveEvaluatedTransform`, which only resolves top-level scene-children) ‚Üí a nested child's gizmo sits detached by the parent transform ([[H116]]); the seed is fixed but the drag still writes proxy-world verbatim as local params ‚Üí dragging a nested child double-applies the parent and jumps WORSE (the two halves MUST move together); the manipulator is re-attached to the real rendered three object instead of the synthetic proxy ‚Üí the evaluated/animated-clone decoupling the proxy exists for is lost; the parent world is recomputed on every `onObjectChange` frame instead of captured once at seed time (a full render-root eval per drag-frame); a non-uniform parent scale + rotated child writes a sheared local matrix a TRS decompose can't represent (an accepted limit ‚Äî matches Blender). Type: STRUCTURAL (one pure parent-world resolver, two directions: seed-from-world + write-to-local). Sibling of [[V37]] (viewport==render), [[V59]] (world transform is pure), [[H40]] (one band, two callers), [[H116]] (the detached-gizmo diagnosis), [[V67]]/[[H115]] (the transformable Group that made nesting live).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#230, 2026-06-22, `ux-overhall` `043cb8b`). `resolveParentWorldMatrix` + `walkParent`/`isIdentityMatrix` (resolveWorldTransform.ts); Gizmo.tsx world-anchor seed (`localTRSMatrix`) + `worldToLocalTRS` write-back, parent world captured in a ref at seed time. Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest **1883** (+6 unit). OBSERVED (live boundary-pair): nested cube under Group@[5,1,0] ‚Üí gizmo seed [5,1,0] (was [0,0,0]), world drag [8,1,0] ‚Üí local [3,0,0]; top-level cube grab [2,0,0] ‚Üí param [2,0,0] byte-identical. e2e `tests/e2e/p230-nested-gizmo-world.spec.ts`; p7.3/gltf-group-gizmo/p209/p210/gizmo-autokey regression green. KNOWN-LIMITS: glTF-child world (name-addressed) keeps the local path; non-uniform-parent-scale+rotated-child shear; nested snap in local space; second render-root eval per seed (cache-share follow-up).

## V69 ‚Äî A node's user-facing name is `meta.name`, mutated ONLY through the `setMeta` op; every rename surface funnels through ONE inline editor + ONE op so outliner/inspector/render/undo agree [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #224]

**The invariant:** a node's display label is `meta.name` (resolved by the ONE function `nodeDisplayName` = `meta.name ?? params.name ?? id`, `src/app/sceneTreeWalk.ts`). It lives on `node.meta`, OUTSIDE the per-type `paramSchema`, so `setParam` cannot touch it ‚Äî renaming is its own first-class op `setMeta { nodeId, name? }` (`src/core/dag/ops.ts` `applySetMeta`): writes `meta.name`, preserves other meta fields (graph `position`), normalizes an emptied meta back to `undefined` (a renamed-then-cleared node is byte-identical to one never named), and `name: undefined` CLEARS the override so the label falls back to the id. Its inverse is a `setMeta` restoring the prior name (undo round-trips). Every rename TRIGGER ‚Äî outliner row double-click, inspector-header double-click, F2 shortcut ‚Äî funnels through ONE shared inline editor (`RenameInput`) and ONE coordinating store (`renameStore { nodeId, scope }`), so at most one editor is open and F2 from anywhere targets the active node without two surfaces fighting for focus. This is the [[V34]] single-identity rule for naming + the [[H40]]-style "one write authority, N surfaces" shape.

**Breaks when:** a surface writes `meta.name` directly (not via the op) ‚Üí undo/activity-log/agent-closure miss it; a rename seeds the editor from `nodeDisplayName` (the id, for an unnamed node) instead of the raw `meta.name` ‚Üí committing unchanged BAKES the id in as a name; two surfaces both render an autofocusing editor for the same node (no `scope` discriminator) ‚Üí focus war; a new op type is added to the union but `opTargetNodeId` (`src/agent/closure/expand.ts`, the only exhaustive `switch(op.type)` with no default) isn't extended ‚Üí tsc exhaustiveness break (the compiler catches it ‚Äî that's the design); a new bg-/text- token (`bg-bg-0`) is introduced for the editor instead of reusing an already-audited pair (`text-fg` on `bg-bg-2`) ‚Üí the contrastMatrix coverage-gate fails (use an audited token or add a ROW). Type: STRUCTURAL (one identity channel, one op, N triggers). Sibling of [[V34]] (one substrate), [[V65]] (one shared select handler ‚Äî same "one rule, N callers" shape), [[H40]] (one band, two callers).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#224, 2026-06-22, `ux-overhall` `1a70666`+`7439d3e`, 2 slices). Slice 1 `1a70666` (core `setMeta` op: types union + `applySetMeta` + closure-gate case + 6 unit incl. inverse round-trip; `meta.name` already in NodeSchema ‚Üí no migration). Slice 2 `7439d3e` (`renameStore` + `RenameInput` shared editor; SceneTree dbl-click; NPanel header IS the editable name now, raw id+type beneath; KeyboardShortcuts F2 ‚Üí outliner rename of primary). Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest **1889**. OBSERVED (live, `tests/e2e/p224-rename.spec.ts` 3 e2e): outliner dbl-click + F2 + inspector-header rename each write `meta.name`, display reflects it, undo restores, Escape cancels with no write. KNOWN-LIMITS: F2 needs the target's outliner row VISIBLE (collapsed glTF subtree / narrow-mode hidden outliner ‚Üí F2 sets renaming but no input mounts ‚Äî harmless, overwritten next time); no name-uniqueness enforcement (duplicates fine ‚Äî id + icon disambiguate, Blender's `.001` suffix not replicated); rename works uniformly on wrapper/Scene-root/glTF-child nodes (harmless); no agent `rename` mutator yet (op exists + closure-gated, a clean follow-up).

## V70 ‚Äî The selected SET is the unit of action: the gizmo transforms the whole set about a shared median pivot, the inspector edits set-on-all; both derive from `selectedNodeIds` (not just `primaryNodeId`), and the per-node world delta EXTENDS V68 [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #225]

**The invariant:** when >1 node is selected, downstream surfaces act on the SET, not the active node alone. (1) **Gizmo** ‚Äî `Gizmo()` is a dispatcher: >1 manipulable selected ‚Üí `MultiGizmo` (else `SingleGizmo`, byte-identical to pre-#225). `MultiGizmo` seeds ONE proxy at the MEDIAN (average) of the selected nodes' WORLD positions and, each `onObjectChange`, applies the proxy's incremental world transform to EVERY node about that shared pivot: `delta = proxyWorld ¬∑ seedProxyWorld‚Åª¬π`, each node `newWorld = delta ¬∑ seedWorld(node)`, then `newWorld ‚Üí LOCAL params` via `matrixToLocalTRS` (the matrix sibling of [[V68]]'s `worldToLocalTRS`). Per-node `seedWorld` from `resolveWorldTransform`, parent from `resolveParentWorldMatrix` ‚Äî so nesting composes correctly. Translate = the same world delta on all; rotate/scale orbit each node about the median AND transform it (Blender "median point"). (2) **Inspector** ‚Äî `NPanel` branches on `selectedNodeIds.size`: >1 ‚Üí `MultiSelectInspector` (an "N objects selected" summary + the shared Transform section, wiring the previously-dead `MULTI_SELECT_SECTIONS`). Each axis shows the value shared across selected nodes that own the param, or "‚Äî" (mixed); editing dispatches ONE atomic `setParam` batch over the whole set ‚Üí one undo. This is the [[V65]] "one rule, N callers" shape applied to ACTION (the set), and the [[V68]] world‚Üîlocal round-trip applied to the SET.

**Breaks when:** a consumer reads `primaryNodeId` where it should read `selectedNodeIds` (the set goes inert again ‚Äî the #225 starting bug); the multi gizmo writes proxy-world verbatim as each node's params (skips the per-node `parentWorld‚Åª¬π` / pivot strip ‚Üí nested nodes double-apply the parent, exactly the [[H116]] failure √óN); the median pivot is recomputed mid-drag from the moving nodes instead of captured once at seed (the pivot drifts as nodes move); a mutation closure captures the render-scope node list instead of reading LIVE state (an Enter-then-blur double-commit fires a second atomic whose inverse ‚Äî computed against already-updated state ‚Äî is a no-op, so undo can't revert ‚Äî the bug found+fixed in `MultiSelectInspector.setAxis`); the single‚Üîmulti split is put INSIDE one component body via an early return (rules-of-hooks violation ‚Äî it MUST be a dispatcher choosing sub-components). Type: STRUCTURAL (the selected set as the action unit). Sibling of [[V65]] (one shared select handler ‚Äî the SELECTION side of the same set), [[V68]] (the manipulator round-trip this extends per-node), [[V34]] (one substrate), [[H40]] (one band, N consumers).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#225, 2026-06-22, `ux-overhall` `4860cf7`+`b5c19f7`, 2 slices). Slice 1 `4860cf7` (inspector: `MultiSelectInspector` set-on-all + NPanel count branch; the live-state read fix). Slice 2 `b5c19f7` (gizmo: `Gizmo` dispatcher + `MultiGizmo` median-pivot delta + `matrixToLocalTRS`). Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest **1889**. OBSERVED live: inspector ‚Äî 2 boxes, mixed x shows "‚Äî", edit x=7 ‚Üí both 7, one undo ‚Üí [0,3] (`p225-multi-edit.spec.ts`); gizmo ‚Äî median [2,0,0], translate Œî[3,0,0]‚Üí[3,0,0]/[7,0,0], rotate 90¬∞Y about median‚Üí[2,0,2]/[2,0,-2]+rot90 (`p225-multi-gizmo.spec.ts`); single-node regression green (p230/p7.3/p209/p210/gltf-group/autokey). KNOWN-LIMITS (v1): multi gizmo writes PLAIN setParam ‚Äî no per-node animated-route/autoKey/GltfChild-override-flag, no snapping (preserves relative spacing); animated nodes may not follow a multi-drag; only an explicit `scale` band is multi-scaled (never geometry `size`); a drag is many undo entries (coalesce = follow-up); inspector multi-edit writes the static source (animated nodes may show no change ‚Äî multi-keyframing is a later slice); box-select to BUILD a set is #226 (today the set comes from shift-click / the `selectMany` seam); pivot is median-average only (the `viewportStore.pivot` modes are #228).

## V71 ‚Äî Marquee (box) selection projects each object's WORLD ORIGIN through the live camera and tests origin-in-rect; it reuses the ONE shared world resolver (so a box hits an object where it RENDERS) and stays a UI projection that never touches the DAG [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #226]

**The invariant:** box-select decides membership by projecting each selectable object's WORLD ORIGIN (`resolveWorldTransform(state,id,ctx).position`, the SAME pure resolver the gizmo seeds from ‚Äî one band, [[H40]]/[[V37]]) through the live editor camera to screen px and testing whether that point falls inside the drawn marquee AND in front of the camera (NDC z ‚â§ 1). Blender object-mode parity: the ORIGIN is tested, not the full screen bounds. The geometry is a PURE core (`src/viewport/boxSelect.ts` ‚Äî `normalizeRect`/`rectContains`/`isDragRect`/`boxSelectHits`) with the projector INJECTED, so it unit-tests without THREE; the real perspective projection is observed in the e2e boundary-pair (`__basher_box_select_project`). The selectable UNIVERSE is `getViewportSelectableIds` (scene `children` + `lights` + active `camera` ‚Äî every kind `resolveWorldTransform` reaches). The interaction is a TRANSIENT MODAL armed by `B` (it does NOT hijack LMB-drag, which stays Basher's primary orbit gesture): a DOM crosshair overlay captures the drag + draws the marquee, the in-Canvas controller owns projection + commit, Shift-box ADDS to the set, a replace-box on empty CLEARS, Esc/RMB/click-without-drag CANCEL, and one box per `B` press (Blender idiom). Like every selection write it goes through `useSelectionStore` only ‚Äî a UI projection, never the DAG ([[V1]]/[[V8]], the same contract `selectNodeOnClick` keeps).

**Breaks when:** the hit test reads a LOCAL transform (`resolveEvaluatedTransform`, top-level only) or the raw `params.position` instead of `resolveWorldTransform` ‚Üí a nested/animated object is boxed where it's AUTHORED, not where it renders ([[V37]]/[[H40]] violated, same class as [[H116]]); the projector forgets the in-front-of-camera gate (NDC z>1) ‚Üí objects BEHIND the camera whose projection wraps into the rect get falsely selected; `B` is bound to LMB-drag-on-empty instead of a modal ‚Üí it fights OrbitControls (Basher orbits on LMB, unlike Blender's MMB) and the "drag to orbit" affordance breaks; the overlay doesn't guard `onPointerMissed` while active ‚Üí the underlying missed-click CLEARS the set the box is about to fill; the marquee introduces a new `bg-`/`text-` token for its fill ‚Üí the W8 contrast coverage-gate fails (it's a non-text transient ‚Üí use INLINE rgba, no token obligation); box-select mutates the DAG (writes a node, a transient) instead of only `selectMany` ‚Üí [[V1]]/[[V8]] violation. Type: STRUCTURAL (one world-origin projector, one selectable universe, a transient modal that never touches the DAG). Sibling of [[V65]] (one shared select handler ‚Äî the click side of selection), [[V68]]/[[V59]] (the world resolver this projects through), [[V70]] (the SET this fills, consumed by the multi-gizmo/inspector), [[H40]] (one band, N consumers).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#226 Slice 1, 2026-06-22, `ux-overhall` `4a8bd04`). Pure `boxSelect.ts` (+8 unit) + `selectableNodes.ts` (`getViewportSelectableIds`) + `boxSelectStore` (UI-only modal) + `BoxSelectController` (in-Canvas projection+commit, DEV seams `__basher_box_select`/`__basher_box_select_project`) + `BoxSelectOverlay` (DOM crosshair + marquee) + KeyboardShortcuts `B`/Esc-cancel + Viewport `onPointerMissed` guard. Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest **1897**. OBSERVED live (`tests/e2e/p226-box-select.spec.ts` 6/6): projection of n_box/n_box_b origins, box‚Üísingle (active reassigned), box‚Üíboth, Shift-box‚Üíadd, replace-box-on-empty‚Üíclear, B arms overlay + Esc cancels, and a REAL pointer drag draws the marquee + selects both (screenshot). **#226 COMPLETE** (all 3 slices shipped): Slice 1 box-select (`4a8bd04`), **Slice 2 outliner ctrl/shift multi-select** (`400734e` ‚Äî `SceneTree.onRowClick` modifier-aware + active-ring vs member-fill styling), **Slice 3 shortcut parity** (`a8c05b7` ‚Äî USER chose Blender-pure: bare-`A`=Select-All, Add‚ÜíShift+A only; Alt+A=Deselect; Ctrl/Cmd+I=Invert; all over the full `getViewportSelectableIds` universe; MenuBar Select menu relabelled). KNOWN-LIMITS (v1): only `B`-modal BOX (no lasso/circle ‚Äî the issue's optional follow-ups); origin-in-rect (an object whose body overlaps the box but whose origin is outside is NOT hit ‚Äî Blender's default, no "whole object" mode); box/select-all catch the camera+lights too (correct Blender parity) which the multi-gizmo then includes.

## V72 ‚Äî Scene-node structural mutations (delete / duplicate / reparent) are pure op-BUILDERS that disconnect-before-removeNode and re-wire edges among fresh ids; ONE shared authority (`sceneNodeActions`) feeds every surface so the keyboard and the menu can't drift [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #227]

**The invariant:** every structural change to the scene graph ‚Äî delete, duplicate, reparent ‚Äî is expressed as a list of the op-union primitives (`addNode`/`removeNode`/`connect`/`disconnect`) built by a PURE function of `(DagState, ids)`, dispatched as ONE atomic (‚Üí one undo), with the actual selection/state mutation left to the caller. Two ordering rules make these undo-safe and consumer-safe: (1) **disconnect-before-removeNode** ‚Äî `removeNode` REFUSES while a node's output is still consumed (`ops.ts applyRemoveNode`), so `buildDeleteNodesOps` disconnects every consumer edge first; (2) **addNode(empty inputs) ‚Üí connect internal edges ‚Üí connect root-to-parent** for duplicate, so the inverse (disconnect, then removeNode) never hits a still-consumed node. Duplicate FOLLOWS only the hierarchy sockets (`children`, wrapper `target`) to gather the subtree, mints deterministic `<id>_copy` ids (uniqueness-checked against `state.nodes`, no `Date.now`/`Math.random` ‚Üí unit-testable), re-points internal edges to the clones, and keeps every NON-hierarchy input (material, geometry) SHARED with the original. Reparent = `disconnect(old parent socket) + connect(new Group/Scene children, append)`, cycle-guarded by the outliner row-key PATH (`dst.key.startsWith(src.key + '/')`). ONE module `src/app/sceneNodeActions.ts` holds the delete + duplicate builders so the Delete KEY, Shift-D, and the outliner context menu all dispatch the SAME ops ‚Äî the [[V65]]/[[V69]] "one write authority, N callers" shape applied to structural edits. Selection stays a UI projection (V1/V8); these builders never touch selection.

**Breaks when:** a surface inlines its own delete/duplicate loop instead of calling the shared builder ‚Üí the two drift (the context-menu Delete differs from the Delete key); a duplicate emits `addNode` WITH inputs (or connects before all clones exist) ‚Üí undo's `removeNode` fails because a clone is still consumed (the disconnect hasn't run yet); a reparent connects the new edge before disconnecting the old, or forgets the cycle guard ‚Üí a node parented into its own descendant (infinite render / orphaned subtree); duplicate FOLLOWS a non-hierarchy edge (clones a shared material) ‚Üí the copy desyncs from the original instead of co-editing; fresh ids use `Date.now()`/`Math.random()` ‚Üí non-deterministic, untestable, and (in a workflow script) a thrown call. Type: STRUCTURAL (one shared op-builder authority; disconnect-before-remove ordering; hierarchy-only subtree walk). Sibling of [[V65]] (one shared select handler), [[V69]] (the setMeta rename op + one editor), [[V1]]/[[V8]] (DAG mutation only via Op; selection is projection), [[V71]] (the box-select that fills the set these act on).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#227 Slices 1‚Äì3, 2026-06-22, `ux-overhall` `c27e0b6`‚Üí`01ceb2b`). S1 reparent-drag `c27e0b6` (SceneTree `reparentSocket`/`canReparent`/`onDrop`; `p227-reparent-drag` 4/4). S2 context menu `417d743` (`buildDeleteNodesOps` shared with the Delete key; portalled menu Rename/Duplicate/Select-Hierarchy/Delete; capture-phase Esc; `p227-context-menu` 5/5). S3 duplicate `01ceb2b` (`buildDuplicateNodeOps` + Shift-D + ctx Duplicate; +5 unit; `p227-duplicate` 2/2). Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest **1902**. KNOWN-LIMITS: multi-select duplicate/reparent act on one node only (the primary / dragged); duplicate doesn't copy `meta` (copy shows its id ‚Äî Blender `.001` non-goal); reparent only of `children`-socket rows (wrapper `target` children inert). **S5 outliner ergonomics SHIPPED (2026-06-22) ‚Üí [[V73]]** (Group/Transform/Material collapse + scroll-to/expand-to selection + arrow-key nav). REMAINING #227: only S4 visibility (decided: `node.meta.hidden` per-object + renderer skip).

## V73 ‚Äî Outliner collapse is ONE projection mechanism: visible rows = the pre-order tree walk with every collapsed container's subtree cut by ROW-KEY PREFIX; collapse is pure UI state (never the DAG); ancestors auto-expand on selection; keyboard nav follows the ARIA roving-tabindex tree pattern [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #227 S5]

**The invariant:** the outliner's visible-rows list is the full `buildSceneTreeRows` pre-order walk, minus the descendants of any COLLAPSED container, identified in ONE pass by `row.key.startsWith(cutKey + '/')` (the row key IS the parent-path, so a descendant's key nests under its ancestor's ‚Äî the same prefix relation the cycle guard and Select-Hierarchy use). A row owns a chevron iff a later row's key nests under it (`rowsWithChildren`, computed once from the pre-order list) AND its type is collapsible (`Group`/`Transform`/`MaterialOverride`/`GltfAsset`). Two defaults, one cut: glTF assets default COLLAPSED (opt-in `expandedAssets`, the D-05 node-flood guard); the wrapper containers default EXPANDED (opt-out `collapsedNodes`). All collapse state is local component UI ‚Äî it NEVER mutates the DAG (the rows + their nodes still exist; only the projection hides them; [[V1]]/[[V8]]). On `primaryNodeId` change (e.g. a viewport pick), every collapsed ancestor of the active row auto-expands (ancestors = rows whose key strictly prefixes the active row's key) so the row surfaces, then it scrolls into view; the expand setters return the SAME set reference when nothing changes so the effect can't loop. Keyboard nav is the ARIA tree pattern with ROVING TABINDEX: only the active row is tab-reachable (Scene root when nothing is selected), arrows move the active row (Up/Down = prev/next visible, Right = expand-or-step-into-first-child, Left = collapse-or-step-to-parent), Enter/Space (re)select; a `navByKeyboard` flag makes the move FOCUS the row (not just scroll); the focused row owns these keys (`stopPropagation` before the window shortcut handler) so Space selects rather than toggling playback.

**Breaks when:** a second collapse mechanism is added (e.g. a per-type expanded set keyed by node id) instead of the one key-prefix cut ‚Üí glTF and wrapper collapse drift, and a node that appears under two keys collapses inconsistently; the cut tests node id instead of row KEY ‚Üí a node projected at two tree positions collapses both (the key is position-unique, the id is not); collapse writes to the DAG (a `hidden`/`collapsed` param) instead of local UI state ‚Üí a pure view preference corrupts the document + breaks undo ([[V1]]/[[V8]]); the auto-expand effect's setters allocate a new Set unconditionally ‚Üí the `[primary, allRows]` effect re-renders ‚Üí re-runs ‚Üí infinite loop; keyboard keys don't `stopPropagation` ‚Üí Space on a focused row ALSO toggles global playback (the window keydown handler is bubble-phase, below which React's stopPropagation halts the native bubble); the chevron button keeps `tabIndex=0` ‚Üí Tab lands on chevrons between rows, breaking roving-tabindex nav. Type: STRUCTURAL (one projection-cut by key prefix; collapse is UI not DAG; roving-tabindex tree). Sibling of [[V72]] (the structural op-builders these rows act on ‚Äî collapse is the VIEW side, those are the WRITE side), [[V65]] (the click-select handler this nav reuses via `select`), [[V1]]/[[V8]] (DAG mutation only via Op; the tree is a projection, [[V34]] single identity via `nodeDisplayName`).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#227 Slice 5, 2026-06-22, `ux-overhall` 5a/5b/5c + self-review). 5a generalized collapse to Group/Transform/MaterialOverride via the unified key-prefix cut + `rowsWithChildren` (`p227-collapse` 2/2); 5b scroll-to/expand-to on selection (`p227-scroll-to` 1/1); 5c arrow-key nav with roving tabindex (`p227-arrow-nav` 1/1, incl. Space-doesn't-toggle-playback). Self-review removed the now-dead `TreeRow.gltfAssetOwner` (the key-prefix cut superseded the glTF-only owner back-reference). Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest **1902**; glTF node-flood + child-addressing e2e stayed green (glTF children still collapse ‚Äî their key nests under the asset's). KNOWN-LIMITS: collapse state is per-session local (not persisted to the project); Scene root isn't collapsible; arrow Enter/Space collapse a multi-selection to the single focused row; no type-ahead / Home-End jump.

## V74 ‚Äî Per-object visibility is a `meta.hidden` flag toggled by a dedicated `setHidden` op; the renderer SKIPS a hidden node by rendering null IN ITS SLOT (index-correspondence preserved); the offscreen render shares the live scene so viewport==render (one band); the eye lives ONLY where the skip is honored [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #227 S4]

**The invariant:** an object's visibility is `node.meta.hidden` (absent/false = visible ‚Äî the default, so no migration; identity/view data on `meta`, not a per-type param, because every node kind hides uniformly ‚Äî like `meta.name`). It is toggled by a DEDICATED `setHidden { nodeId, hidden }` op (NOT an `OpSetMeta` field: setMeta's `name: undefined` means CLEAR, so one op can't say "set hidden, leave name untouched"); apply deletes the key on `false` (an unhidden node is byte-identical to one never hidden ‚Üí minimal save diffs), preserves other meta, and round-trips through undo. The renderer (`SceneFromDAG`) skips a hidden TOP-LEVEL child by returning `null` IN ITS `children.map` SLOT ‚Äî it does NOT filter the array, so index `i` still corresponds to `childRefs[i]` (the band invariant the direct-channel / constraint / click-select maps rely on; [[V37]]/[[H40]]). Because the offscreen still (#168) and animation (#189) render capture the SAME live three.js scene, a node absent from the live scene is absent from the render too ‚Äî ONE band, no separate render-exclusion denylist. The outliner eye appears ONLY on the rows the renderer actually skips by source-node-id (depth-1, the Scene's direct children) so the affordance can NEVER lie; clicking it dispatches the op (one undo, `stopPropagation` so it doesn't select), dims the row + flips the glyph to eye-off, and the eye stays visible while hidden so the way back is never lost.

**Breaks when:** the renderer FILTERS the hidden child out of `value.scene.children` (or shifts indices) instead of rendering null in-slot ‚Üí `childRefs[i]` desyncs from `children[i]` and DirectChannelsR / ConstrainedR / click-to-select route to the wrong node (the same index-correspondence class as [[V71]]); the eye is shown on a row whose node the renderer does NOT skip (a nested depth>1 row in v1) ‚Üí toggling it sets `meta.hidden` but the object stays rendered ‚Äî the affordance LIES; visibility is stored OUTSIDE `meta.hidden` (a Scene-level hidden-set, a per-type param) ‚Üí it doesn't round-trip through save/undo with the node, or it can't apply uniformly across node kinds; `setHidden` is folded into `setMeta` ‚Üí the `name:undefined`-clears semantics collide (no way to set hidden without touching name); the offscreen render rebuilds its own scene graph instead of capturing the live one ‚Üí hidden nodes reappear in the render (viewport‚âÝrender, [[V37]] violated). Type: STRUCTURAL (visibility on the substrate via a dedicated op; null-in-slot render skip preserving index-correspondence; one-band viewport==render; affordance only where honored). Sibling of [[V72]] (the structural op-builders ‚Äî this is the visibility op beside delete/duplicate/reparent), [[V73]] (the outliner rows this eye sits on), [[V37]]/[[H40]] (one band, the live scene IS the render), [[V71]] (the index-correspondence the null-in-slot skip protects). KNOWN-LIMITS (v1): top-level rows only (nested hide = follow-up); a hidden node selected from the outliner still seeds a floating gizmo (the gizmo reads the pure resolver, not the mesh); no keyboard `H` hide path (the eye is `tabIndex=-1`); multi-select hide is a follow-up.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#227 Slice 4, 2026-06-22, `ux-overhall` ‚Äî 4.1 op `setHidden`+`meta.hidden` + 4.2 renderer-skip + outliner eye). +5 ops unit (apply/inverse/normalize/undo round-trip/throw) + `p227-visibility` e2e 2/2 (eye hides in live scene + DAG-retained + undo restores + click-doesn't-select). Observed live (screenshot): hidden row dimmed with eye-off glyph, box gone from the viewport, selection unchanged. Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest **1907**. **#227 outliner parity COMPLETE** (S1 reparent ¬∑ S2 context-menu ¬∑ S3 duplicate ¬∑ S4 visibility ¬∑ S5 ergonomics).

## V75 ‚Äî Viewport CLICK selection is nearest-SURFACE occlusion picking (the frontmost geometry the ray hits ‚Üí its addressable LEAF node), NEVER nearest-origin; hierarchy is traversed by EXPLICIT affordance (Alt+click selects up, Select Hierarchy, outliner), never broad-first drill. Origin-in-region is the BOX/marquee rule ONLY [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #233, replaces the UX#7 drill model]

**The invariant (target):** a single viewport click selects the LEAF object whose visible surface is under the cursor ‚Äî the frontmost ray intersection (`e.intersections[0]`, depth-sorted nearest-first; R3F already raycasts), mapped to its addressable DAG node (for a glTF, the `GltfChild` under the cursor via `nodeNameMap` ‚Äî exactly what `buildGltfDrillChain` already computes as `chain[last]`). It is NOT the top-level asset/group, and it is NOT chosen by which node's ORIGIN is nearest the cursor. Selecting the whole asset / a parent is an EXPLICIT act: **Alt+click selects UP** the hierarchy one level (the inverse of today's drill-in; `chain` toward `chain[0]`), plus the outliner and the shipped **Select Hierarchy** (#227 S2). **Repeat-click at the same pixel CYCLES** through overlapping hits front-to-back (the `e.intersections` order). This mirrors Blender Object Mode: GPU ID-buffer occlusion picking (`gpu_select` / `DRW_select_buffer_find_nearest_to_point`) selects the frontmost drawn object; hierarchy is the explicit _Select Grouped ‚Üí Parent/Children_ / _Select More/Less_ operators (bundled manual `scene_layout/object/selecting.rst`), never implicit on click. The SAME band stays surface-based for click and ORIGIN-based for box-select ([[V71]] ‚Äî Blender box-select tests the object origin against the region in object-center mode; the two operations differ in Blender too).

**Breaks when:** click selection picks by nearest ORIGIN instead of nearest surface ‚Üí the cursor is a RAY not a 3D point, so origin-proximity (a) selects an object when the click is over EMPTY SPACE near its pivot, and (b) on overlap picks by pivot distance instead of what's visibly in front ‚Äî wrong winner whenever a part's geometry sits far from its own/shared origin (see [[H117]]); click stays broad-first (selects the asset/group) ‚Üí the user must drill to reach the part they pointed at (the friction this replaces); the leaf-map diverges from `buildGltfDrillChain`'s `nodeNameMap` derivation ‚Üí click selects a different node than the outliner/gizmo address ([[H104]]/V34 single-identity); origin-in-region logic leaks from box-select ([[V71]]) into click, or surface-logic leaks into box-select ‚Üí each operation must keep its own rule. Type: STRUCTURAL (click = nearest-surface leaf-pick; hierarchy = explicit affordance; origin = box-select only). Sibling of [[V71]] (the origin-in-region box rule ‚Äî the deliberate contrast), [[V65]] (the one shared `selectNode` handler this routes through), [[H104]] (the click‚Üíaddressable-node identity), [[V73]] (the outliner Select-Hierarchy / Alt+click affordances that serve the broad case). REPLACES the UX#7 broad-first drill model (`gltfDrillChain.ts` + `drillStore.ts` + `SceneFromDAG` onClick/onDoubleClick + the Esc pop-out in KeyboardShortcuts): drill-IN on double-click is retired; the chain is repurposed for Alt+click select-UP.

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#233, 2026-06-23, `ux-overhall` `5623177`). `SceneFromDAG.tsx` SceneChildNode `onClick` now: `hit = e.intersections[0]?.object ?? e.object` ‚Üí `chain = buildGltfDrillChain(state, pickId, hit)`; plain click ‚Üí `chain[last]` (the leaf; `pickId` when chain ‚â§1, i.e. a non-glTF mesh); **Alt+click** ‚Üí up one level from the current selection's place in the chain (`idx = chain.indexOf(primaryNodeId)`; `chain[Math.max(0, idx-1)]`, or `chain[length-2]` if the current node isn't in this chain), no-op at the root (FORK: user chose no-op-at-root over sibling-cycle). The shared `selectNode` (V65) still owns the write (stopPropagation + shift-additive). RETIRED: the double-click drill-in (`onDoubleClick` prop gone) + the Esc drill pop-out in `KeyboardShortcuts.tsx` (Esc just clears now) + the `drillStore` (DELETED ‚Äî the single-vs-double-click race it guarded is gone; Alt+up derives statelessly from the chain + live selection) + the `onPointerMissed` drill reset in `Viewport.tsx`. KEPT: `buildGltfDrillChain` / `gltfDrillChain.ts` (the leaf-map + up-walk reuse it ‚Äî comments updated UX#7‚Üí#233) + the H90 GltfAssetR clone-stamping. **Repeat-click overlap cycling = follow-up** (FORK: user chose to ship the core first). OBSERVED live (`tests/e2e/p233-leaf-pick-select.spec.ts`, real R3F raycast): single click ‚Üí GltfChild leaf; Alt+click ‚Üí Group up; repeat Alt+click ‚Üí no-op; plain click ‚Üí leaf again; Esc ‚Üí clears. Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest **1902** (‚àí8 = the deleted drillStore unit tests; `gltfDrillChain.test.ts` unchanged-green). Grounded vs the bundled Blender manual (`scene_layout/object/selecting.rst`) + engine ID-buffer picking (`gpu_select`). See [[H117]] (why closest-origin was rejected). KNOWN-LIMITS (v1): no overlap cycling yet; Alt+up at root is a no-op (broader selection = outliner / Select-All); a glTF child's gizmo still keeps the local path (V68 known-limit, unchanged); Alt+Shift+click adds the up-node to the set (acceptable).

## V76 ‚Äî Transform ergonomics (snap-Affect / orientation / pivot / set-origin) are VIEWPORT-PROJECTION state wired into the gizmo through PURE math helpers; the gizmo write-back stays orientation- and pivot-agnostic (it reads the resulting WORLD pose), and every mode is grounded against the Blender manual [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #228]

**The invariant:** the gizmo's transform ergonomics are editor-session projections (`gizmoStore`/`viewportStore`, never the DAG, V8) wired in through PURE, three-light math helpers so they unit-test without a GPU and the gizmo's onObjectChange stays a single write path. The four #228 controls: (1) **snap Affect** ‚Äî `viewportStore.snapAffect {move,rotate,scale}` + per-mode steps; `maybeSnapTransform(mode, value)` is the ONE gate (`snapEnabled && snapAffect[mode] && step>0`), and `maybeSnapVec3` is a translate alias so the move-Affect gate covers the character walk-to path too. (2) **orientation** ‚Äî `gizmoStore.orientation 'global'|'local'` maps to three's `TransformControls.space`; the write-back is UNCHANGED because it reads the resulting proxy WORLD transform (orientation only changes the handle/drag axes, not the dispatched value). (3) **pivot** ‚Äî `viewportStore.pivot` drives the MultiGizmo only (single-node collapses to its own origin); `pivotPoint(mode, origins, active)` (pure) seeds the proxy (median/boundingBox/active), and 'individual' applies only the LINEAR part of the drag delta about EACH node's own origin (translate stays the shared delta ‚Äî pivot-independent, Blender parity). (4) **Set Origin to Geometry** ‚Äî `originToGeometry(params, worldCentre)` (pure) returns position+pivot that move a Group's origin to the content centre while keeping geometry fixed (`pos ‚àí R¬∑S¬∑pivot` invariant); the button reads LIVE scene bounds via `useThreeRef` (the non-Canvas scene access the Render/Frame actions use) and dispatches one atomic. Every mode's semantics are grounded against the bundled Blender manual (`pivot_point/`, `orientation.rst`, `snapping.rst`, `axis_locking.rst`, `origin.rst`).

**Breaks when:** snap logic is inlined per-mode in the gizmo instead of the one `maybeSnapTransform` gate ‚Üí translate and rotate/scale snap drift; orientation is made to alter the write-back (it must only change handle axes ‚Äî the dispatched value comes from the proxy's resulting world pose, V68/H40) ‚Üí a local-space drag double-transforms; pivot mode is read by the SingleGizmo (it's a MULTI concern ‚Äî a single node's median==active==its own origin) ‚Üí needless complexity; 'individual' applies the FULL delta (orbit) instead of the linear part about each origin ‚Üí objects orbit the median in individual mode; Set-Origin moves `position` WITHOUT compensating `pivot` ‚Üí the geometry jumps (the `pos ‚àí R¬∑S¬∑pivot` invariant is the fixity guarantee); a transform control mutates the DAG directly instead of through `gizmoStore`/`viewportStore` (V8) ‚Üí a view preference corrupts the document. Type: STRUCTURAL (viewport-projection state + pure math helpers + one gizmo write path; Blender-grounded). Sibling of [[V68]] (the world‚Üîlocal manipulator round-trip these extend), [[V70]] (the multi-gizmo set these pivot), [[V59]] (the pure world resolver), [[H40]] (one band, read==render).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#228, 2026-06-23, `ux-overhall`, 4 slices). Snap Affect `b0e4f53` (`maybeSnapTransform` + toolbar M/R/S chips + p228-snap-affect.spec.ts + 6 unit). Orientation `6653f06` (`gizmoStore.orientation` ‚Üí `space` + toolbar chip + p228-orientation.spec.ts + 3 unit; screenshot-observed local handles rotate onto the object's axes). Pivot `2ce9351` (`gizmoPivot.ts` `pivotPoint` + MultiGizmo seed + individual linear-about-own-origin + toolbar `<select>` + p228-pivot-modes.spec.ts + 6 unit). Set-Origin `6d462b5` (`setOrigin.ts` `originToGeometry` + pivot‚Üítransform routing + Group-only `SetOriginControl` reading `useThreeRef` bounds + p228-set-origin.spec.ts + 4 unit). Gate tsc0/eslint0/vitest **1921**. DEFERRED ‚Üí #234: per-axis keyboard lock (G‚ÜíX/Y/Z modal-grab ‚Äî Basher's gizmo is drei handle-drag, which already constrains per-axis by grabbing an arrow), 3D cursor pivot, editable rotate/scale snap-step UI, Set-Origin extras (center-of-mass, nested/rotated-parent exactness), local-multi orientation.

## V77 ‚Äî A camera is aimed/rotated by ONE pure (lookAt-point + roll) ‚Üî world-orientation bijection: every consumer derives orientation forward from it, and the camera gizmo writes authored lookAt+roll back through its inverse [IMPLEMENTED ‚Äî #229]

**The invariant:** a Basher camera has NO rotation param ‚Äî it aims via `position` + a `lookAt` POINT + `roll`¬∞ ([[V56]]). The mapping between those authored params and the camera's world ORIENTATION is ONE pure bijection in `src/app/cameraOrientation.ts`: `cameraOrientationQuat(position, lookAt, roll)` (forward: local -Z onto the aim via `Matrix4.lookAt` + world-+Y up, then roll about the view axis) and `lookAtRollFromQuat(quat, position, distance)` (inverse: forward ‚Üí lookAt at the kept distance, plus the signed roll about forward). EVERY surface that turns a pose into an oriented camera derives it FORWARD from `cameraOrientationQuat` ‚Äî the viewport look-through (`applyView`), the frustum helper (`frustumQuaternion` delegates), the still + animation render (`buildRenderCamera`), and the camera world-transform seam (`cameraWorldMatrix`) ‚Äî so render == viewport == helper at any roll (the [[V37]]/[[H40]] one band; there is no second orientation code path to drift). The camera GIZMO (`CameraGizmo`, the dispatcher's 3rd branch beside Multi/Single) manipulates the camera in WORLD orientation and writes authored `lookAt`+`roll` back through the INVERSE ‚Äî the [[V68]] "manipulate in render space, store authored params" round-trip applied to a camera: ROTATE seeds the rotate proxy from `cameraOrientationQuat` and converts the drag back via `lookAtRollFromQuat` (aim distance fixed ‚Üí the aim orbits the camera, the Z-twist banks roll); a second translate AIM handle at the world lookAt point writes `lookAt` directly; TRANSLATE moves `position` only (the lookAt point stays put ‚Üí the camera re-aims at it). `roll` is a camera SCALAR animatable param (`ANIMATABLE_CAMERA_SCALAR_PARAMS`) overlaid by `resolveActiveCameraPoseAt` exactly like fov/near/far, and a first-class TRANSFORM inspector row (keyframeable via the GENERIC diamond ‚Äî it is NOT inside the custom `CameraLensControls`, so it sidesteps the [[H104]] custom-control trap). Every gizmo write funnels through the same `routeAnimatedGrab ‚Üí setParam ‚Üí autoKeyCommit` chokepoint #190 camera authoring uses (V1). Cameras are flat (never nested) so there is NO parent-world round-trip ‚Äî the proxy world IS the camera's world.

**Breaks when:** a consumer orients the camera with its own `lookAt`/`setFromUnitVectors` instead of `cameraOrientationQuat` ‚Üí it ignores roll (or twists differently) and viewport ‚âÝ render at any bank ([[V37]] break, the pre-#229 state where `frustumQuaternion` used a twist-free arc); the gizmo seeds the rotate proxy from a raw euler instead of the orientation quaternion ‚Üí the inverse recovers the wrong lookAt/roll; the rotate write does NOT keep the seeded aim distance ‚Üí the lookAt slides toward/away as you spin (the aim should ORBIT); a partial/legacy pose carries an `undefined`/NaN roll and the forward math does `degToRad(roll)` unguarded ‚Üí the whole quaternion becomes NaN and the camera vanishes ([[H118]] ‚Äî finite-guard roll ‚Üí 0); `roll` is added to the custom `CameraLensControls` instead of left as a generic transform row ‚Üí it re-inherits the [[H104]] missing-diamond trap; the camera gizmo writes `position` AND `lookAt` on translate (Blender object-translate semantics) when the model is "lookAt point stays put" ‚Üí the aim no longer holds on the subject. Type: STRUCTURAL (one bijection, N forward consumers + one inverse for the manipulator). Sibling of [[V56]] (the camera pose authority it orients), [[V68]] (the world‚Üîauthored manipulator round-trip it is the camera instance of), [[V60]] (the Track-To aim that DERIVES lookAt ‚Äî complementary to this direct write), [[V37]]/[[H40]] (one band, render==viewport==helper).

**Status:** IMPLEMENTED (#229, 2026-06-23, `ux-overhall`, 3 slices).
